Substitution in Ijarah: Stipulated Personal Work vs. Absolute Permission
Ruling on substitution in ijarah with proof and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios in ijarah regarding substitution and apply the Hanafi ruling that absolute permission allows hiring a substitute while personal work stipulation prohibits it.

Core Idea
If the contract stipulates personal work, the worker may not substitute; if unqualified, he may hire another because the work is a debt in his liability.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question in ijarah contracts: can a hired worker use someone else to do the work? The Hanafi school distinguishes between two scenarios: when the employer explicitly requires the worker to perform personally, and when no such condition is made. Understanding this distinction is crucial for both employers and workers in service contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contractual scenarios
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between a contract that stipulates personal work (e.g., 'work yourself') and one that is unconditional (mutlaq). The ruling pivots on this condition.
The Arabic phrase 'شرط عمله بنفسه' indicates a stipulation for personal performance.
2
Locate the proof for the ruling
The passage states: 'لأن المعقود عليه العمل في محل بعينه كالمنفعة في محل بعينه' (because the contracted work is in a specific place like benefit in a specific place). When the work is tied to the person, it cannot be delegated. When unqualified, the work is a debt (dayn) in the worker's liability, which can be fulfilled by a substitute.
The proof is based on the nature of the obligation: specific vs. generic.
3
Note the exception for the wet nurse
The passage mentions an exception in al-Khulasa for a wet nurse (ظئر) who is allowed to use a substitute. This is a special case due to her circumstances.
The exception is based on necessity or custom.
4
Distinguish between hiring and mere delegation
The commentary clarifies that with absolute permission, the worker may hire another but not simply hand over the work. Hiring creates a subsidiary contract, while delegation without a separate contract is not allowed.
The phrase 'له أن يستأجر غيره' (he may hire another) implies a formal engagement, not a gratuitous transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يستعمل غيره أن شرط عمله بنفسه لأن المعقود عليه العمل في محل بعينه كالمنفعة في محل بعينه. واستثنى في الخلاصة الظئر فإن لها أن تستعمل غيرها. والمراد من اشتراط العمل بنفسه أن يقول له اعمل بنفسك أو بيدك ولا تفعل بيد غيرك كما في الخلاصة. أما إذا قال على أن تعمل فهو من قبيل ما إذا أطلق؛ كذا في المستصفى وغاية البيان. وفي الخلاصة : رجل استأجر رجلين ليحملا له خشبة إلى منزله بدرهم فحمل أحدهما دون الآخر فله نصف درهم وإن لم يكونا شريكين في العمل قبل ذلك، وكذا لو استأجر أحدهما لبناء حائط أو حفر بئر ولو كانا شريكين يجب كل الأجر بينهما. وقيد باشتراط العمل لأنه لو اشترط عليه أن يعمل اليوم أو غداً فلم يفعل فطالبه صاحبه مرات ففرط حتى سرق لا يضمن، وأجاب شمس الإسلام بالضمان؛ كذا في الخلاصة قوله : (وإن أطلق كان له أن يستأجر غيره لأن المستحق عمل في ذمته ويمكن استيفاؤه بنفسه وبالاستعانة بغيره بمنزلة إيفاء الدين. وأشار بكونه له الاستئجار إلى أنه ليس له الدفع إلى غيره ولهذا قال في الخلاصة : رجل دفع غزلاً إلى رجل لينسجه كرباساً فدفع هو إلى آخر لينسجه فسرق من يده إن كان الثاني أجيراً للأول لا يضمن واحد منهما، وإن كان الثاني أجنبياً ضمن الأول دون الآخر عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما في الأول ضامن مطلقاً، وفي الأجنبي إن شاء ضمن الأول وإن شاء ضمن الأخر
His saying: (He does not use another if he stipulated his own work) because the contracted work is in a specific place like the benefit in a specific place. An exception is made in al-Khulasa for a wet nurse, for she may use another. The meaning of stipulating work himself is that he says to him 'work yourself or with your hand and do not do it with the hand of another' as in al-Khulasa. As for if he says 'on condition that you work', it is of the same category as when he gives absolute permission; thus in al-Mustasfa and Ghayat al-Bayan. In al-Khulasa: A man hired two men to carry a log to his house for a dirham, and one carried it without the other, so he gets half a dirham even if they were not partners in the work before that. Similarly, if he hired one of them to build a wall or dig a well, and if they were partners, the entire wage is between them. He restricted it to stipulation of work because if he stipulated that he work today or tomorrow, and he did not do it, and the owner demanded from him several times, and he neglected until it was stolen, he is not liable. Shams al-Islam gave a ruling of liability; thus in al-Khulasa. His saying: (And if he gave absolute permission, he may hire another) because what is due is work in his liability (dhimma), and it can be fulfilled by himself or by seeking help from another, like paying a debt. He indicated by saying he may hire another that he may not hand it over to another, and for this reason it is said in al-Khulasa: A man gave wool to a man to weave it into cloth, and he gave it to another to weave, and it was stolen from his hand. If the second was an employee of the first, neither is liable. If the second was a stranger, the first is liable but not the other according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first is absolutely liable, and regarding the stranger, if he wishes he can hold the first liable or the other.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrases 'ولا يستعمل غيره' and 'وإن أطلق'. The commentary first explains that if the contract stipulates the worker must do the work himself, he cannot use a substitute because the contracted subject is work in a specific place, similar to a specific benefit. An exception is made for a wet nurse (ظئر) who may use a substitute due to her special situation. The meaning of stipulating personal work is explicit wording like 'work yourself' or 'do not let another do it'. If the employer says 'on condition that you work', it is treated as absolute permission, so the worker may hire a substitute. The commentary then provides examples: hiring two men to carry a log—if one carries alone, he gets half the wage unless they were partners before. A condition for work on a specific day with neglect leads to non-liability for theft, but Shams al-Islam ruled liability. For the case of absolute permission, the worker may hire another because the work is a debt on his liability, and fulfilling it through a substitute is like paying a debt. However, he cannot delegate to another without hiring, as shown in the cloth-weaving example. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises: if the second worker is a stranger, according to Abu Hanifa only the first worker is liable, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the first is liable in either case and the employer can choose whom to sue for the stranger case.

Key Terms
ظئر (thu'l): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.
مطلق (mutlaq): Unqualified or absolute permission in the contract, without stipulation of personal work.
أجير (ajir): A worker hired for a specific task; in this context, an employee of the first worker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a worker is hired with absolute permission and he hires a substitute to do the work?
A) It is not allowed because work is personal.
B) It is allowed, and the substitute is directly liable to the employer.
C) It is allowed, but the original worker remains liable for the work.
D) It is allowed only if the employer consents.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah, if the contract stipulates personal work, substitution is prohibited; if unqualified, substitution by hiring is allowed but the original worker remains liable.

Liability Dispute in Ijarah: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Substitution by a Stranger
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on liability when a substitute is a stranger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability when a hired worker delegates to a stranger and apply the mufta bihi view in fatwa.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds only the first worker liable; Sahibayn hold both liable, giving the employer a choice of whom to sue.

This lesson dives into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding liability when a hired worker, under absolute permission, passes the work to a stranger (ajnabi) without a formal hiring contract, and the property is stolen. Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on who bears the loss. Understanding their proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah) is essential for accurate fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Recall the scenario from the passage
The scenario: a man gives wool to a weaver to weave into cloth. The weaver gives it to a stranger to weave, and it is stolen. The question is: who is liable?
The weaver is the first worker (ajir), the stranger is ajnabi.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: the first worker is liable; the stranger is not liable. The first worker is at fault for delegating without authorization, and the stranger is considered his agent, so only the principal (first worker) is liable.
Proof: the first worker breached trust by giving it to an unauthorized person; the stranger is not directly accountable to the employer.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the first worker is absolutely liable in all cases; and regarding the stranger, the employer may choose to hold either the first worker or the stranger liable. They see the stranger as acting without any authority from the employer, thus both are responsible.
Proof: the stranger took possession without proper authority, so he is a usurper (ghasib) in relation to the employer.
4
Analyze the difference in proof
Abu Hanifa views the stranger as a sub-agent, so only the principal is liable. Sahibayn view the stranger as an independent wrongdoer because he had no contract with the employer, thus the employer can pursue either.
Key point: whether the stranger is an agent of the first worker or a stranger to the employer.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, the employer can only sue the first worker. According to Sahibayn, he can sue the first worker in any case, and also the stranger if he wishes. This gives the employer more flexibility and protection.
The mufta bihi today is the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يستعمل غيره أن شرط عمله بنفسه لأن المعقود عليه العمل في محل بعينه كالمنفعة في محل بعينه. واستثنى في الخلاصة الظئر فإن لها أن تستعمل غيرها. والمراد من اشتراط العمل بنفسه أن يقول له اعمل بنفسك أو بيدك ولا تفعل بيد غيرك كما في الخلاصة. أما إذا قال على أن تعمل فهو من قبيل ما إذا أطلق؛ كذا في المستصفى وغاية البيان. وفي الخلاصة : رجل استأجر رجلين ليحملا له خشبة إلى منزله بدرهم فحمل أحدهما دون الآخر فله نصف درهم وإن لم يكونا شريكين في العمل قبل ذلك، وكذا لو استأجر أحدهما لبناء حائط أو حفر بئر ولو كانا شريكين يجب كل الأجر بينهما. وقيد باشتراط العمل لأنه لو اشترط عليه أن يعمل اليوم أو غداً فلم يفعل فطالبه صاحبه مرات ففرط حتى سرق لا يضمن، وأجاب شمس الإسلام بالضمان؛ كذا في الخلاصة قوله : (وإن أطلق كان له أن يستأجر غيره لأن المستحق عمل في ذمته ويمكن استيفاؤه بنفسه وبالاستعانة بغيره بمنزلة إيفاء الدين. وأشار بكونه له الاستئجار إلى أنه ليس له الدفع إلى غيره ولهذا قال في الخلاصة : رجل دفع غزلاً إلى رجل لينسجه كرباساً فدفع هو إلى آخر لينسجه فسرق من يده إن كان الثاني أجيراً للأول لا يضمن واحد منهما، وإن كان الثاني أجنبياً ضمن الأول دون الآخر عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما في الأول ضامن مطلقاً، وفي الأجنبي إن شاء ضمن الأول وإن شاء ضمن الأخر

أجير (ajir): A worker hired for a specific task; in this context, the first worker.
أجنبي (ajnabi): A stranger, not an employee of the first worker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in this passage, what options does the employer have if his property is stolen after being given to a stranger by the hired worker?
A) He can only sue the hired worker.
B) He can sue the stranger but not the hired worker.
C) He can sue either the hired worker or the stranger, or both.
D) He cannot sue anyone because the property was not in his possession.

Key Takeaway
In the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability when a stranger is subcontracted without authorization, the mufta bihi is that the employer may hold either the original worker or the stranger liable.

Proportionate Wage When Some Family Members Die During Hire
Commentary on a matn regarding wage apportionment in ijara.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wage payment when some hired persons die and explain the condition of specification (ma'lumeen vs. unknown).

Core Idea
If part of the contracted subject is fulfilled, partial wage is due; full wage if the subjects were unspecified.

When an employer hires a worker to bring his family members, what happens if some die en route? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on whether the family members were specifically known. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring (ijara) to bring family members. The ruling: if some die, the worker gets a proportionate wage for the ones he brings.
Proportionality depends on whether the family members are known or unknown.
2
Locate the dalil
The reason (talil) is that he partially performed the contracted subject (ma‘qud ‘alayhi), so he deserves partial compensation.
This is a principle of apportionment in contracts.
3
Note the condition
If the family members are known (specified individually or by count), the wage is proportional. If unknown, the full wage is due because the contract is for the whole task.
This distinction is from al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن استأجره ليجيء بعياله فمات بعضهم فجاء بما بقي فله أجره بحسابه لأنه أو فى بعض المعقود عليه فيستحق الأجر بقدره ومراده إذا كانوا معلومين ليكون الأجر مقابلاً بجملتهم، وإن كانوا غير معلومين يجب الأجر كله إليه أشار في الهداية والله أعلم.
منع الحبس لها شرعاً والألف واللام بدل عن الإضافة تأمل .اهـ. قلت: لا يخفى بعد المعنى الأول هنا بل المراد المتبادر المنع المفهوم من قوله ليس له حق الحبس .
His saying: (And if he hired him to bring his family, and some died, and he brought the remaining, he has his wage in proportion) because he fulfilled part of what was contracted, so he deserves the wage in proportion. His intention is that if they were known (specific individuals), so the wage corresponds to the whole group. If they were unknown, the entire wage is due, as indicated in al-Hidayah. And Allah knows best. The prohibition of detention for it legally, and the 'alif lam' stands for the possessive case. Consider. End quote. I say: It is not hidden that the first meaning is far, rather the apparent meaning is the prohibition understood from his saying 'he has no right of detention'.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on a matn verse about hiring someone to bring one's family members. The ruling states that if some family members die during the journey and the worker brings the remaining, he is entitled to a proportionate wage. The reasoning is that he partially performed the contracted subject. The commentary clarifies a condition: if the family members are known (i.e., specified by number or identity), the wage is proportional because the total wage corresponds to the entire group. If they are unspecified, the full wage is due. This distinction is pointed out in al-Hidayah. The second part of the passage appears to be a marginal note discussing the preceding ruling about detention (likely the runaway slave or a related issue). It cites a saying 'he has no right of detention' and analyzes the grammatical construction, preferring an interpretation that indicates prohibition rather than negation of right. This is a scholarly refinement.

Key Terms
معقود عليه (ma'qud 'alayhi): The subject matter of the contract, i.e., bringing the family members.
معلومين (ma'lumeen): Known or specified family members (e.g., by name or number).
أجر بحسابه (ajr bi-hisabihi): A wage proportional to the part of the work performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of hiring to bring family members, if some die and the worker brings the rest, when is the full wage due?
A) When the family members are known.
B) When the family members are unknown.
C) Always proportional.
D) Never full wage.

Key Takeaway
In ijara, if part of the hired task is performed due to external cause, the worker is entitled to proportionate compensation, provided the subject matter was specified.

Leasing Houses and Shops Without Specifying Use
Commentary on permissibility of ijarah without specifying use.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing houses and shops without specifying the use, explain why it is valid, and identify the permissible activities for the tenant.

Core Idea
A house lease defaults to residence; no need to state use because the benefit is uniform.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes that leasing houses and shops is valid even without specifying the intended use. The commentary explains that the default customary use is residence, which is uniform and not subject to significant variation. The author then expands to list permissible activities and contrasts this with items like garments where specification is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Locate the statement 'صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها'. This is the core ruling: the lease is valid without specifying the use.
The ruling is from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary states 'لأن العمل المتعارف فيه السكني فينصرف إليه وأنه لا يتفاوت'. The reason is that the customary use is residence, which does not vary significantly, so the contract is valid.
This is based on custom (urf) and the uniformity of the benefit.
3
Note the scope and exceptions
The ruling applies to houses and shops, but not to garments or animals where use varies. The tenant may reside himself or sublet, and may perform various activities like wudu, bathing, light pounding, etc.
Activities are limited to customary and non-harmful uses.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
The Hanafi position is that specification is not required; the Shafi'i school requires specification to avoid gharar. Contrast the two positions.
The practical difference: Hanafi deems contract valid from start, Shafi'i deems it fasid unless use is specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
۵۱۷
إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو
باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
قوله : (صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها لأن العمل المتعارف فيه السكني فينصرف إليه وأنه لا يتفاوت فصح العقد، والحوانيت الدكاكين؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وأشار إلى أنه لا يشترط أيضاً بيان من يسكنها فله أن يسكنها بنفسه ويسكنها غيره بإجارة وغيرها، وكذا من استأجر عبداً للخدمة له أن يؤجره لغيره بخلاف الدابة والثوب؛ كذا في القنية وقيد بالدور والحوانيت لأن الثوب لا بد من بيان ،لابسه وكذا كل ما يختلف باختلاف المستعمل فله الوضوء والاغتسال وغسل الثياب وكسر الحطب المعتاد والاستنجاء بحائطه والدق المعتاد اليسير وأن يتد وتداً وربط الدواب في موضع معتاد له لا إن لم يكن معتاداً، وله ربطها على باب الدار وليس للآجر أن يدخل دابته الدار المستأجرة؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي القنية : لمستأجر الدار المسيلة إلقاء ما اجتمع من كنس الدار من التراب إن لم يكن له قيمة وله أن يتد فيه وتداً ويستنجي بجداره ويتخذ فيه بالوعة إلا إذا كان فيه ضرر بين، ولو استأجر حانوتاً مسبلاً لدق الأرز له ذلك إن لم يضر بالبناء، وليس لمستأجر الدار المسبلة أن يجعلها إصطبلاً .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان فيها ماء توضأ منها وشرب ولو فسدت البئر لا يجبر أحدهما على إصلاحها، ولو بنى المستأجر التنور في الدار المستأجرة فاحترق شيء من الدار لم يضمن المستأجر قوله : (إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً) فيه وجهان: الأوّل أن يكون بفتح الياء من الثلاثي المجرد فيكون انتصاب «حداداً» وما بعده على الحال ويفهم منه عدم إسكانه غيره دلالة بالأولى الثاني أن يكون بضم الياء وكسر الكاف وانتصاب ما بعده على المفعولية، ويفهم منه عدم سكناه بنفسه بالإشارة لأنه إنما لم يجز أن يسكن غيره لأن ذلك يوهن البناء وفي سكنى نفسه ملتبساً بهذه الأشياء هذا المعنى حاصل؛ كذا في غاية البيان. وهذا إذا لم يرض به المالك أو لم يشترطه في الإجارة، فإن استأجره لذلك كان له ذلك، ولو اختلفا في الاشتراط فالقول للمؤجر كما لو أنكر أصل العقد، وإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة المستأجر ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي القنية: استأجر حانوتاً مسبلاً لدق الأرز له ذلك إن لم يضر بالبناء .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : وإذا استأجر ليقعد قصاراً فله أن يقعد حداداً إذا كان مضرتهما واحدة والمراد من الرحى غير رحى اليد، أما رحى اليد فلا يمنع
باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
قوله : (أما رحى اليد الخ فيه سقط والذي في الخلاصة لا يمنع من رحى اليد إن كان لا يضر وإن كان يضر يمنع وعليه الفتوى .
Chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what is disputed. 517. Leasing houses and shops without stating what will be done in them, except that a blacksmith, fuller, or miller may not reside. Chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what is disputed. His saying: (The leasing of houses and shops is valid without stating what will be done in them) because the customary use is residence, so the contract is valid. Shops are stores; thus in al-Jawhara. He indicated that it is also not necessary to state who will reside, so the tenant may reside himself or let others reside by ijarah or otherwise. Similarly, one who hires a slave for service may sublet him, unlike an animal or garment; thus in al-Qunyah. He restricted it to houses and shops because a garment requires specifying the wearer, and likewise everything that varies with the user. So the tenant may perform wudu, bathe, wash clothes, break customary firewood, clean himself against the wall, do light customary pounding, insert a peg, tie animals in a customary place (if not customary, not allowed), tie them at the door. The lessor may not bring his animal into the rented house; thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Qunyah: The tenant of a leased house may throw away the dirt collected from sweeping if it has no value, may insert a peg, clean himself against its wall, dig a cesspool unless it causes clear harm. If he rents a shop for pounding rice, he may do so if it does not harm the building. The tenant of a public house may not turn it into a stable. In al-Khulasa: If there is water, he may perform wudu from it and drink; if the well becomes spoiled, neither is forced to repair it. If the tenant builds an oven in the rented house and something catches fire, the tenant is not liable. His saying: (Except that he does not reside as a blacksmith, fuller, or miller). There are two interpretations: First, that the ya' is fatha from the triple root (yasqunu), so 'blacksmith' etc. are in the accusative as state (hal), implying he does not allow others to reside, a fortiori. Second, that the ya' is damma and the kaf is kasra (yuskinu), and the accusative is as object, implying that he himself does not reside (i.e., he does not live there), because he may not allow others to reside as that weakens the building, and residing himself with these occupations has the same effect; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. This applies if the owner does not consent or it was not stipulated in the contract; if he rented for that purpose, it is allowed. If they dispute the stipulation, the owner's word is taken, as if he denied the contract. If both produce evidence, the lessee's evidence is stronger; thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Khulasa: If he rents to sit as a fuller, he may sit as a blacksmith if the harm is the same. What is meant by mill is not the hand mill; as for the hand mill, it is not prevented. Chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what is disputed. His saying: (As for the hand mill) there is a gap. What is in al-Khulasa: it is not prevented if it does not cause harm; if it does, it is prevented, and the fatwa is upon that.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the permissibility of certain ijarah contracts and points of disagreement. The main ruling states that leasing houses and shops is valid without specifying the use, because the default is residence, which is uniform. Shops (دكاكين) are included. The tenant may reside himself or sublet, unlike hiring a garment which requires specifying the wearer. The commentary then lists permissible uses: wudu, bathing, washing clothes, breaking firewood, cleaning against the wall, light pounding, inserting a peg, tying animals in customary places. The lessor may not bring his own animal. The tenant may dispose of valueless dirt, dig a cesspool if no clear harm, and rent a shop for rice pounding if no structural damage. Turning a public house into a stable is prohibited. Water in the property may be used; well spoilage does not force repair. If a tenant builds an oven and fire damages the property, he is not liable. The matn includes an exception: the tenant may not reside as a blacksmith, fuller, or miller. The commentary gives two grammatical interpretations, both leading to a prohibition on these trades, whether by the tenant or others, due to potential damage to the building. If the owner consented or the contract was for that purpose, it is allowed. In case of dispute, the owner's word is taken, but the lessee's evidence is stronger. If the harm is equal, one trade may replace another. The hand mill is not prohibited unless it causes harm, and the fatwa is based on that.

Key Terms
حوانيت (hawaneet): Plural of حانوت, meaning shops or stores.
مسبلة (musabbala): A house or shop leased for public benefit (waqf or free use).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default ruling on leasing a house without specifying the use?
A) Invalid due to ambiguity.
B) Valid, and the tenant may reside or sublet.
C) Valid only for the tenant's own residence.
D) Requires the owner's permission for any use.

Key Takeaway
Leasing a house or shop is valid without specifying use because the default benefit (residence) is uniform and known by custom.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
7 min
Prohibited Occupations in Rented Property: Blacksmith, Fuller, and Miller
Exception clause on prohibited trades in rented houses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three prohibited occupations in a rented house, state the condition for their permissibility, and apply the rule to analogous trades.

Core Idea
A tenant cannot use a rented house for damaging trades like blacksmithing unless the owner consents.

This lesson examines the exception in the matn: the tenant may not reside as a blacksmith, fuller, or miller. The commentary explores the rationale—these occupations weaken the building—and clarifies that the prohibition is not absolute; it depends on the owner's consent or contractual stipulation. It also discusses how to handle disputes and the special case of the hand mill.

Guided Path
1
State the prohibition
Identify the phrase 'إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً'. This is an exception to the general validity of the lease.
These are heavy trades: blacksmith (haddad), fuller (qassar), and miller (tahan).
2
Understand the two grammatical interpretations
The commentary provides two readings of the verb 'يسكن': one implying he does not allow others to reside (fatha reading), the other implying he himself does not reside (damma reading). Both lead to the same prohibition.
The difference in interpretation does not affect the ruling; both prohibit these trades.
3
Identify the rationale
The reason is that these occupations 'يوهن البناء' (weaken the building). The harm is the common factor.
The prohibition is not merely etiquette; it is based on preventing damage.
4
Note the exceptions
The prohibition applies only if the owner did not consent or it was not stipulated in the contract. If the owner rents for that purpose, it is allowed. Disputes over stipulation are settled by the owner's word, but the lessee's evidence is stronger if both present proof.
This gives flexibility while protecting the owner's property.
5
Apply to analogous trades
The commentary mentions that if the harm is the same, one trade can replace another (e.g., fuller to blacksmith). Also, the hand mill is not prohibited unless it causes harm, and the fatwa follows that ruling.
This shows a case-by-case evaluation based on harm.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Leasing Houses and Shops Without Specifying Use
Ruling on validity of leasing houses/shops without specifying use, with exception of certain professions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing a house without specifying use, identify the exceptional professions that require the lessor's consent, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving harmful or customary uses.

Core Idea
A lease is valid without specifying use because custom points to residence; harmful professions need consent.

This lesson examines a key question in Hanafi ijarah: can you lease a house or shop without detailing its exact use? The Hanafi school says yes, basing this on custom (urf). However, some professions are so harmful to the property that they require special permission. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the default ruling, the exceptions, and the practical consequences for both lessor and lessee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is leasing a house or shop. The ruling: the lease is sahih (valid) even without specifying the use, because the customary use is residence.
This is based on the principle that urf determines the intended usufruct.
2
Understand the role of custom (urf)
Custom (urf) fills in the missing specification. For houses, the default is residence; for shops, the default is whatever is customary for that type of shop.
Custom must be uniform and not vary significantly.
3
Recognize the exceptional professions
Three professions are singled out: blacksmith (haddad), fuller (qassar), and miller (tahhan). They are prohibited unless the lessor consents because they cause excessive load, vibration, fire, or water damage.
The prohibition applies even if not explicitly stated in the contract.
4
Analyze the two grammatical readings
The Arabic phrase 'except that he does not house a blacksmith...' can be read two ways: one prohibiting the lessee from allowing others (e.g., subletting) and the other prohibiting the lessee himself from engaging in that work. Both are understood to be prohibited.
The reliance is on the meaning, not the grammatical form.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Consider hand-mill vs. large mill, subleasing, and incidental uses (e.g., drawing water, tying animals). The hand-mill is allowed if no harm; subleasing is allowed if no additional restriction; incidental uses are generally permitted unless they cause clear harm.
Fatwa distinguishes between harmful and non-harmful uses.

باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو
قوله : (صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها لأن العمل المتعارف فيه السكني فينصرف إليه وأنه لا يتفاوت فصح العقد، والحوانيت الدكاكين؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وأشار إلى أنه لا يشترط أيضاً بيان من يسكنها فله أن يسكنها بنفسه ويسكنها غيره بإجارة وغيرها، وكذا من استأجر عبداً للخدمة له أن يؤجره لغيره بخلاف الدابة والثوب؛ كذا في القنية وقيد بالدور والحوانيت لأن الثوب لا بد من بيان ،لابسه وكذا كل ما يختلف باختلاف المستعمل فله الوضوء والاغتسال وغسل الثياب وكسر الحطب المعتاد والاستنجاء بحائطه والدق المعتاد اليسير وأن يتد وتداً وربط الدواب في موضع معتاد له لا إن لم يكن معتاداً، وله ربطها على باب الدار وليس للآجر أن يدخل دابته الدار المستأجرة؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي القنية : لمستأجر الدار المسيلة إلقاء ما اجتمع من كنس الدار من التراب إن لم يكن له قيمة وله أن يتد فيه وتداً ويستنجي بجداره ويتخذ فيه بالوعة إلا إذا كان فيه ضرر بين، ولو استأجر حانوتاً مسبلاً لدق الأرز له ذلك إن لم يضر بالبناء، وليس لمستأجر الدار المسبلة أن يجعلها إصطبلاً .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان فيها ماء توضأ منها وشرب ولو فسدت البئر لا يجبر أحدهما على إصلاحها، ولو بنى المستأجر التنور في الدار المستأجرة فاحترق شيء من الدار لم يضمن المستأجر قوله : (إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً) فيه وجهان: الأوّل أن يكون بفتح الياء من الثلاثي المجرد فيكون انتصاب «حداداً» وما بعده على الحال ويفهم منه عدم إسكانه غيره دلالة بالأولى الثاني أن يكون بضم الياء وكسر الكاف وانتصاب ما بعده على المفعولية، ويفهم منه عدم سكناه بنفسه بالإشارة لأنه إنما لم يجز أن يسكن غيره لأن ذلك يوهن البناء وفي سكنى نفسه ملتبساً بهذه الأشياء هذا المعنى حاصل؛ كذا في غاية البيان. وهذا إذا لم يرض به المالك أو لم يشترطه في الإجارة، فإن استأجره لذلك كان له ذلك، ولو اختلفا في الاشتراط فالقول للمؤجر كما لو أنكر أصل العقد، وإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة المستأجر ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي القنية: استأجر حانوتاً مسبلاً لدق الأرز له ذلك إن لم يضر بالبناء .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : وإذا استأجر ليقعد قصاراً فله أن يقعد حداداً إذا كان مضرتهما واحدة والمراد من الرحى غير رحى اليد، أما رحى اليد فلا يمنع
قوله : (أما رحى اليد الخ فيه سقط والذي في الخلاصة لا يمنع من رحى اليد إن كان لا يضر وإن كان يضر يمنع وعليه الفتوى .
من الطحن عليها وإن كان يضر وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في الخلاصة ولو فعل ما لا يجوز له وجب عليه الأجر، وإن انهدم البناء بعمله وجب عليه الضمان ولا أجر لما علم أنهما لا يجتمعان. قيد بالدور والحوانيت لأن استئجار البناء وحده لا يجوز في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا ينتفع بالبناء وحده. وفي القنية يفتى برواية جواز استئجار البناء إذا كان منتفعاً به كالجدر إن السقف اهـ. وفي الجوهرة المستأجر إذا أجر بأكثر مما استأجر تصدق بالفضل إلا إذا أصلح فيها شيئاً أو أجرها بخلاف جنس ما استأجر والكنس ليس بإصلاح. وفي الجوهرة: وإن أجرها من المؤجر لم يجز سواء كان قبل القبض أو بعده، وهل هو نقض للعقد الأوّل؟ فيه اختلاف المشايخ والأصح أن العقد ينفسخ .

فاسدة
Chapter: What is permissible in Ijarah and what is disputed therein. Leasing houses and shops without specifying what work is done in them, except that a blacksmith or fuller or miller is not housed. He said: (It is valid to lease houses and shops without specifying what work is done in them, because the customary use is residence, so it is referred to that, and it does not vary, so the contract is valid. Shops are stores; thus in al-Jawhara. And he indicated that it is also not required to specify who resides in them, so he may reside in it himself and let others reside in it by ijarah or otherwise. Similarly, one who hires a slave for service may sub-hire him to another, unlike an animal or garment; thus in al-Qunyah. And it is restricted to houses and shops because a garment requires specification of its wearer, and similarly everything that differs with the difference of user. So he has the right to perform wudu, bathe, wash clothes, break customary firewood, clean himself with its wall, light pounding, drive a peg, and tie animals in a customary place, not if it is not customary. He may tie them at the door of the house, and the tenant may not bring his animal into the rented house; thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Qunyah: The tenant of a mosquelike house may throw away accumulated sweeping dust if it has no value, and he may drive a peg, clean himself with its wall, and make a drain unless it causes clear harm. If he rents a mosquelike shop for pounding rice, he may do so if it does not harm the building, and the tenant of a mosquelike house may not make it a stable. In al-Khulasa: If there is water in it, he may perform wudu from it and drink; if the well becomes spoiled, neither is compelled to repair it. If the tenant builds an oven in the rented house and something of the house burns, the tenant is not liable. He said: (Except that he does not house a blacksmith or fuller or miller) has two aspects: first, that it is with fatha of the ya from the simple triliteral, so 'blacksmith' and what follows are in the accusative as hal, and it is understood from it that he does not let others reside, by more pressing indication. Second, that it is with damma of the ya and kasr of the kaf, and what follows is in the accusative as maf'ul, and it is understood from it that he does not reside himself by indication, because he only did not permit housing others because that weakens the building, and in his own residence while engaged in these things, this meaning is obtained; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. This is if the owner is not pleased or did not stipulate it in the ijarah; if he rents for that, he may do so. If they dispute over the stipulation, the word is of the lessor, as if he denied the contract; if they produce evidence, the evidence of the tenant prevails; thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Qunyah: If one rents a mosquelike shop for pounding rice, he may do so if it does not harm the building. In al-Khulasa: If he rents to sit as a fuller, he may sit as a blacksmith if their harm is the same. And by 'mill' is meant other than the hand-mill; as for the hand-mill, it is not prevented. He said: (As for the hand-mill, there is an omission in the text, and what is in al-Khulasa is that the hand-mill is not prevented if it does not cause harm; if it causes harm, it is prevented, and upon it is the fatwa. From grinding upon it even if it causes harm, and upon it is the fatwa; thus in al-Khulasa. If he does what is not permissible, the rent is due; if the building collapses due to his action, he is liable for damages and there is no rent, because it is known that they do not combine. It is restricted to houses and shops, because leasing a building alone is not permissible in Zahir al-Riwayah, since one cannot benefit from the building alone. In al-Qunyah, fatwa is given on the permissibility of leasing a building if it is beneficially usable, like walls and ceiling. In al-Jawhara: If the tenant leases at more than he rented, he should give the excess in charity, unless he made some improvement or leased it for a different genus of consideration; sweeping is not an improvement. In al-Jawhara: If he leases it back to the lessor, it is not permissible, whether before or after possession; is this a dissolution of the first contract? There is disagreement among the scholars, and the correct view is that the contract is annulled.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the permissibility of leasing houses and shops without specifying the exact use. The ruling: the lease is valid, because the customary use is understood to be residence. The lessee can use it for residence, and can even sublet it without the lessor's permission. However, an exception is made for occupations that cause excessive load or vibration: a blacksmith, fuller, or miller may not be housed unless the lessor agrees. The commentator discusses two possible readings of the Arabic—whether it means the lessee himself may not engage in such work or he may not allow others to do so. The relied-upon view is that both are prohibited without consent, but if the tenant does so, the lease remains valid and the full rent is due, but any damage caused must be compensated. The passage also covers incidental uses: the lessee may perform wudu, wash clothes, drive pegs, tie animals in customary places, etc. Additional rulings include: if a well in the property spoils, neither party is compelled to repair; if the tenant builds an oven and fire damages the house, the tenant is not liable unless negligent. The hand-mill is treated less strictly than a large mill—permitted if no harm. The passage concludes with a note that leasing a building alone (without land) is invalid in Zahir al-Riwayah, but a later fatwa permits it if the building is usable. Subleasing at a profit is allowed only if the tenant adds value; otherwise, the excess should be given in charity.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of leasing or hiring, transferring usufruct (manfa'ah) for a known consideration.
حداد (haddad): Blacksmith; a profession considered harmful to the building due to hammering and fire.
قصار (qassar): Fuller or launderer; a profession involving water and beating, potentially damaging.
طحان (tahhan): Miller; operates a mill (especially large) causing vibration and dust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone rents a house without specifying the use, and then houses a blacksmith, what happens?
A) The lease becomes void because the use was not agreed.
B) The lease is valid but the tenant must obtain the lessor's permission for the blacksmith.
C) The tenant may not house a blacksmith under any circumstances.
D) The tenant may house a blacksmith without permission as long as he pays extra rent.

Key Takeaway
A lease of a house or shop is valid without specifying use because custom defines it, but harmful professions like blacksmithing require the lessor's explicit consent to protect the property.

Leasing Land for Agriculture: Specifying the Crop
Ruling on necessity to specify crop when leasing land for agriculture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying the crop in an agricultural land lease and apply it to scenarios where the crop is unspecified or delegated.

Core Idea
Specification of crop prevents dispute; if unspecified, planting validates the lease and the full rent is due.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a practical issue in ijarah: when leasing land for farming, the crop must be specified or the choice delegated to avoid uncertainty. The ruling demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh balances contractual clarity with flexibility, allowing the contract to become valid upon actual use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that when leasing land for agriculture, the tenant must either specify the crop (bayan) or delegate the choice to himself (e.g., 'I will plant whatever I wish'). This is essential to avoid future disputes due to ignorance.
If not specified, the contract is initially fasid (defective).
2
Understand the consequence of planting
If the tenant plants a crop without prior specification, the lease becomes valid (sahih) retroactively, and the full named rent (musamma) is due. This is similar to renting a garment without specifying the wearer: once worn, the contract is valid.
The cure is actual use, not just agreement.
3
Note subsidiary rights
The lessee automatically gets incidental rights necessary for usufruct, such as drinking water for irrigation and access paths. These are not part of sale contracts (where the substance is owned) but are inherent in ijarah.
Compare with sale: in sale, rights do not automatically attach.
4
Apply the rules to special cases
The passage addresses cases where irrigation is delayed or impossible: if cultivation is possible within the lease period, the contract is valid; if the land is completely barren (salty), the lease is void. The rent corresponds to the entire period, not only to actual benefit.
Winter leases are valid if cultivation is possible later.
5
Recognize broader uses of land
Land can be leased for non-agricultural purposes like building, planting trees, or even just sitting and resting. This corrects a common misconception that land ijarah is limited to farming.
Al-Hidayah and Ghayat al-Bayan confirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والأراضي للزراعة أن يبين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء) أي ذلك للإجماع العملي عليه ولا بد من البيان لأنها تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها وما يزرع فيها متفاوت فلا بد من التعيين كيلا تقع المنازعة وترتفع بتفويض الخيرة إليه أيضاً وإلا فهي للجهالة وتنقلب صحيحة بزرعها ويجب المسمى لارتفاعها كاستئجار ثوب لم يبين لابسه إذا ألبس شخصاً انقلبت صحيحة، وكذا الدابة والقدر للطبخ وللمستأجر الشرب والطريق لأنها تنعقد للانتفاع ولا انتفاع إلا بهما فيدخلان تبعاً بخلاف البيع لأن المقصود منه ملك الرقبة لا الانتفاع في الحال حتى جاز بيع الجحش والأرض السبخة دون إجارتها إلا بذكر الحقوق والمرافق كما عرف في البيوع. وفي القنية : استأجر أرضاً سنة على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء فله يزرع فيها زرعين ربيعياً وخريفياً. وفي الجوهرة ولا بأس باستئجار الأرض للزراعة قبل ريها إذا كانت معتادة للري في مثل هذه المدة التي عقد الإجارة عليها، وإن جاء من الماء ما يزرع به بعضها فالمستأجر بالخيار إن شاء نقض الإجارة كلها، وإن شاء لم ينقضها وكان عليه من الأجر بحساب ما روى منها اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو استأجرها ولا يمكنه الزراعة في الحال لاحتياجها إلى السقي أو كري الأنهار أو مجيء الماء فإن كان بحال تمكن الزراعة في مدة العقد جاز وإلا فلا كما لو استأجرها في الشتاء تسعة أشهر ولا يمكن زراعتها في الشتاء جاز لما أمكن في المدة، أما إذا لم يمكن الانتفاع بها أصلاً بأن كانت سبخة فالإجارة فاسدة، وفي مسألة الاستئجار في الشتاء يكون الأجر مقابلاً بكل المدة لا بما ينتفع به فحسب. وقيل: بما ينتفع به اهـ. واعلم أن الأرض لا ينحصر استئجارها للزراعة للبناء والغرس كما يوهمه المتون فقد صرح في الهداية بأن الأرض تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها. وقال في غاية البيان: أراد بغير الزراعة البناء والغرس وطبخ الآجر والخزف ونحو ذلك من سائر الانتفاعات بالأرض اهـ. فإذا عرفت ذلك ظهر لك صحة الإجارات الواقعة في زماننا من أنه تستأجر الأرض مقيلاً ومراحاً قاصدين بذلك إلزام الأجرة بالتمكن منها مطلقاً، سواء شملها الماء وأمكن زراعتها أو
His saying: (And lands for agriculture, that he specify what he will plant in it, or he said: on condition that he plants in it whatever he wishes) meaning that this is by practical consensus, and specification is necessary because it is rented for agriculture and other things, and what is planted in it varies, so specification is necessary to avoid dispute, and it is also resolved by delegating the choice to him. Otherwise, it is for ignorance, and it becomes valid by planting it, and the named rent is due for its rise, like one who rents a garment without specifying its wearer: if he clothes a person, it becomes valid. Similarly, an animal and a pot for cooking, and the lessee has the right to drink and the road, because the contract is concluded for usufruct, and there is no usufruct except by them, so they enter as subsidiary, unlike sale, because its purpose is ownership of the substance, not immediate usufruct, such that selling a small donkey and salty land is permissible without mentioning rights and facilities, as known in sales. In al-Qunyah: If one rents land for a year on condition that he plants whatever he wishes, he may plant two crops: spring and autumn. In al-Jawhara: There is no harm in renting land for agriculture before it is irrigated if it is customarily irrigated within such a period as the lease is contracted for; and if enough water comes to irrigate some of it, the lessee has the option: if he wishes, he may cancel the entire lease, or he may not cancel it and pay rent in proportion to what was irrigated. In al-Qunyah: If he rents it and cannot cultivate it immediately due to need for irrigation or digging canals or water arrival, then if it is possible to cultivate within the lease period, it is permissible; otherwise not, as if he rents it in winter for nine months and cannot cultivate in winter, it is permissible because it is possible within the period. As for if he cannot benefit from it at all, like if it is salty, the ijarah is void. In the issue of renting in winter, the rent corresponds to the entire period, not only to what is benefited from. It is said: to what is benefited from. Know that renting land is not limited to agriculture; for building and planting, as the texts might imply. Indeed, al-Hidayah states that land is rented for agriculture and other things. Ghayat al-Bayan said: By other than agriculture, he meant building, planting, baking bricks, pottery, and similar other benefits from the land. So if you understand that, the validity of leases occurring in our time becomes clear: that one rents land for sitting and resting, intending thereby to make the rent obligatory simply by being able to use it absolutely, whether water covers it and cultivation is possible or not.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage deals with leasing land for agriculture. The key ruling: the tenant must either specify what crop he will plant or grant the lessor discretion (e.g., 'I will plant whatever I wish'). If the tenant plants something else, the contract becomes valid and the full named rent is due, because the specification is for avoiding dispute. The commentator likens this to renting a garment without specifying the wearer: if the tenant uses it, the contract becomes valid. The lessee also gets incidental rights like drinking water and access path. The passage then addresses practical issues: if the land cannot be irrigated initially but can be within the lease period, it is valid; if it is completely barren, the lease is void. A key point: land can be leased for building or other uses, not just farming, contrary to what some texts might suggest. The commentator notes that contemporary leases for mere sitting or resting are valid if the parties intend making rent due by mere availability of use, even if cultivation is not possible.

Key Terms
أرض (ard): Land, specifically in the context of ijarah for agricultural or other uses.
زراعة (zira'ah): Agriculture, farming, cultivation of crops.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification or determination of the crop to be planted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person rents land for agriculture without specifying the crop, but then plants wheat, what is the ruling?
A) The lease is void and no rent is due.
B) The lease becomes valid and the named rent is due.
C) The lease is valid only if the lessor approves.
D) The lease is valid but the rent must be renegotiated.

Key Takeaway
A land lease for agriculture is valid with crop specification or delegation; actual planting cures initial uncertainty and the full rent is due.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Key Rulings on Ijarah: Specifying Crop, Hiring a Building, and Subleasing
Introduces chapter and gives initial rulings on ijarah of land and buildings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on specifying the crop in land ijarah, hiring a building alone, subleasing at a profit, and leasing back to the original owner.

Core Idea
Ijarah validity requires known benefit; subleasing profit requires charity unless improvements are made.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents key rulings on ijarah: from specifying the crop in land leases to the permissibility of hiring a building alone. It also addresses the subleasing of property at a higher rent and the effect of leasing back to the owner. Understanding these rules ensures that ijarah contracts are valid and morally sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenarios
List the five distinct issues covered: hiring a washer or miller, leasing land for cultivation, hiring a building alone, subleasing at a profit, and leasing back to the original owner.
Each scenario has a distinct ruling.
2
Extract the default ruling for each
For each scenario, determine the basic hukm: permissible with conditions, impermissible by default, or requiring charity.
Default rulings may have exceptions.
3
Note exceptions and inner madhhab differences
Identify where the text allows exceptions (e.g., improvement in subleasing) or cites ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars (e.g., hiring a building alone).
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by later fatwa.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
For each contested issue, note which view is relied upon for fatwa, as indicated by the text or the editor's commentary.
The text explicitly mentions fatwa in al-Qunyah for hiring a building with benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها قصاراً أو طحاناً والأراضي للزراعة أن يبين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما من الطحن عليها وإن كان يضر وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في الخلاصة ولو فعل ما لا يجوز له وجب عليه الأجر، وإن انهدم البناء بعمله وجب عليه الضمان ولا أجر لما علم أنهما لا يجتمعان. قيد بالدور والحوانيت لأن استئجار البناء وحده لا يجوز في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا ينتفع بالبناء وحده. وفي القنية يفتى برواية جواز استئجار البناء إذا كان منتفعاً به كالجدر إن السقف اهـ. وفي الجوهرة المستأجر إذا أجر بأكثر مما استأجر تصدق بالفضل إلا إذا أصلح فيها شيئاً أو أجرها بخلاف جنس ما استأجر والكنس ليس بإصلاح. وفي الجوهرة: وإن أجرها من المؤجر لم يجز سواء كان قبل القبض أو بعده، وهل هو نقض للعقد الأوّل؟ فيه اختلاف المشايخ والأصح أن العقد ينفسخ . مع صح أن فاسدة
Book of Ijarah, chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what is invalid in it. [For] a washer or miller and lands for cultivation, that he specify what he will plant in it, or he said: on condition that he plant whatever he wishes of grinding on it even if it harms, and the fatwa is upon it; likewise in al-Khulasa. And if he does what is not permissible for him, the wage is obligatory upon him, and if the building collapses due to his work, he is liable for compensation and no wage, because it is known that they do not combine. Restricted to houses and shops because hiring the building alone is not permissible in the apparent narration because one does not benefit from the building alone. And in al-Qunyah, a fatwa is given on the narration of permissibility of hiring the building if it is beneficial like walls and roof. In al-Jawharah: The lessee, if he leases at more than what he leased, gives the excess in charity, unless he made an improvement in it or leased it for a different genus than what he leased, and sweeping is not an improvement. And in al-Jawharah: And if he leased it from the lessor, it is not permissible whether before or after possession; and is it a cancellation of the first contract? There is difference among the mashayikh, and the most correct is that the contract is annulled.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the chapter on ijarah. First: when hiring a washer or miller, or leasing land for cultivation, the type of crop must be specified. If the lessee does what is not allowed, he must still pay the agreed wage. If his work causes the building to collapse, he is liable for damages and forfeits the wage. Hiring a building alone (without benefit) is invalid unless there is actual benefit as per some narrations. A lessee who subleases at a higher price must give the excess in charity, unless he made improvements or rented for a different type of consideration. Leasing back to the original owner is invalid, and the contract is annulled.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for benefit in exchange for compensation, used here for hiring workers or leasing land/buildings.
قصار (qassar): A washer of clothes, hired for that service.
طحان (tahhan): A miller, hired to grind grain.
إصلاح (islah): Improvement that adds value to the property, exempting the lessee from charity on sublease profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A lessee leases a building and later subleases it at a higher rent without making any improvements. What does the passage require?
A) The sublease is invalid.
B) He must give the excess in charity.
C) He may keep the profit.
D) He must return the excess to the original lessor.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, the benefit must be known and specified; subleasing at a profit triggers a moral obligation to give the excess in charity unless a real improvement is made.

Crop Specification in Land Ijarah
Explains necessity of crop specification and gives subsidiary rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement to specify the crop in land ijarah, explain the role of ijma' 'amali, and apply the rulings to variations in contracts.

Core Idea
Crop specification in land ijarah is required by practical consensus to prevent dispute; omission makes the contract initially fasid but valid upon planting.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the necessity of specifying the crop when leasing land for cultivation. It grounds the requirement in practical consensus (ijma' 'amali) and provides detailed rules for various scenarios, including free choice, seasonal limitations, and alternative uses like building or brick-making.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The passage begins by stating that specifying the crop is necessary, citing ijma' 'amali as the evidence. Note the legal basis for the requirement.
The Hanafi school accepts practical consensus as a valid proof.
2
Understand the consequence of non-specification
If the crop is not specified and no choice is given, the contract is initially fasid (invalid) but becomes sahih (valid) once planting occurs. The lessee must still pay the named rent.
This is analogous to hiring a garment without specifying the wearer.
3
Analyze the subsidiary rulings
The text provides many subsidiary cases: free choice allowing two crops, pre-watering options, winter leases, and complete impossibility (e.g., saline land). For each, trace the logic of validity and rent allocation.
Note the difference between rent for the whole period vs. only the usable period.
4
Expand the scope of land ijarah
The passage emphasizes that land can be leased for non-agricultural purposes like building and brick-making. This counters a possible narrow reading of earlier matns.
Al-Hidayah and Ghayat al-Bayan confirm this broader scope.
5
Evaluate the practical application
The text validates modern practices where land is leased for grazing or resting without specifying cultivation, as long as the contract is not tied exclusively to farming.
This shows the flexibility of Hanafi ijarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والأراضي للزراعة أن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء) أي ذلك للإجماع العملي عليه ولا بد من البيان لأنها تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها وما يزرع فيها متفاوت فلا بد من التعيين كيلا تقع المنازعة وترتفع بتفويض الخيرة إليه أيضاً وإلا فهي للجهالة وتنقلب صحيحة بزرعها ويجب المسمى لارتفاعها كاستئجار ثوب لم يبين لابسه إذا ألبس شخصاً انقلبت صحيحة، وكذا الدابة والقدر للطبخ وللمستأجر الشرب والطريق لأنها تنعقد للانتفاع ولا انتفاع إلا بهما فيدخلان تبعاً بخلاف البيع لأن المقصود منه ملك الرقبة لا الانتفاع في الحال حتى جاز بيع الجحش والأرض السبخة دون إجارتها إلا بذكر الحقوق والمرافق كما عرف في البيوع. وفي القنية : استأجر أرضاً سنة على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء فله يزرع فيها زرعين ربيعياً وخريفياً. وفي الجوهرة ولا بأس باستئجار الأرض للزراعة قبل ريها إذا كانت معتادة للري في مثل هذه المدة التي عقد الإجارة عليها، وإن جاء من الماء ما يزرع به بعضها فالمستأجر بالخيار إن شاء نقض الإجارة كلها، وإن شاء لم ينقضها وكان عليه من الأجر بحساب ما روى منها اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو استأجرها ولا يمكنه الزراعة في الحال لاحتياجها إلى السقي أو كري الأنهار أو مجيء الماء فإن كان بحال تمكن الزراعة في مدة العقد جاز وإلا فلا كما لو استأجرها في الشتاء تسعة أشهر ولا يمكن زراعتها في الشتاء جاز لما أمكن في المدة، أما إذا لم يمكن الانتفاع بها أصلاً بأن كانت سبخة فالإجارة فاسدة، وفي مسألة الاستئجار في الشتاء يكون الأجر مقابلاً بكل المدة لا بما ينتفع به فحسب. وقيل: بما ينتفع به اهـ. واعلم أن الأرض لا ينحصر استئجارها للزراعة للبناء والغرس كما يوهمه المتون فقد صرح في الهداية بأن الأرض تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها. وقال في غاية البيان: أراد بغير الزراعة البناء والغرس وطبخ الآجر والخزف ونحو ذلك من سائر الانتفاعات بالأرض اهـ. فإذا عرفت ذلك ظهر لك صحة الإجارات الواقعة في زماننا من أنه تستأجر الأرض مقيلاً ومراحاً قاصدين بذلك إلزام الأجرة بالتمكن منها مطلقاً، سواء شملها الماء وأمكن زراعتها أو لا، ولا شك في صحته لأنه لم يستأجرها للزراعة بخصوصها حتى يكون عدم ريها فسخاً لها. وفي الولوالجية : استأجر أرضاً ليلبن فيها فالإجارة فاسدة ثم هي على وجهين : إن كان للتراب قيمة ضمن قيمته ويكون اللبن له وإن لم يكن له قيمة فلا شيء عليه واللين له وضمن نقصان الأرض إن نقصت. وفي فتاوى قارئ الهداية أن إجارة الأرض المشغولة بزرع الغير إن كان الزرع بحق بأن كان بإجارة لا يجوز أن تؤجر ما لم يستحصد الزرع إلا أن يؤجرها مضافة إلى المستقبل، وإن كان الزرع بغير مستند شرعي صحت الإجارة لأن الزرع هذه الصورة واجب القلع فإن المؤجر في هذه الصورة قادر على تسليم ما أجره بأن يجبر في صاحب الزرع على قلعه سواء أدرك أم لا، لأنه لا حق لصاحبه في إبقائه اهـ. والدار المشغولة بمتاع الساكن الذي ليس بمستأجر تصح إجارتها وابتداء المدة من حين تسليمها فارغة؛ كذا في القنية وفي الخلاصة ولو أجر الأرض المزروعة ثم سلمها بعدما فرغ وحصد ينقلب جائزاً، ولو قال المستأجر استأجرت منك الأرض وهي فارغة وقال المؤجر لا مشغولة بزرعي يحكم الحال؛ كذا في المنتقى. وفي فتاوى الفضلي: القول قول الآجر
His statement: (And lands for cultivation that he specify what he plants in it or said: on condition that he plant whatever he wishes) i.e., that is due to practical consensus upon it, and specification is necessary because it is leased for cultivation and other things, and what is planted varies, so specification is necessary to prevent dispute, and it is removed by delegating the choice to him as well; otherwise it is due to ignorance and it becomes valid by planting it, and the named rent is obligatory due to its elevation, like hiring a garment without specifying its wearer; if he dresses a person, it becomes valid; similarly an animal and a cooking pot; and the lessee has the right to drink and path because the contract is for benefit and benefit is only with them, so they enter by follow-up, unlike sale because its purpose is ownership of the corpus not immediate benefit, such that selling a donkey and saline land is permissible but leasing it is not except by mentioning rights and facilities as known in sales. And in al-Qunyah: He leased land for a year on condition that he plant whatever he wishes, so he may plant two crops: spring and autumn. And in al-Jawharah: There is no harm in leasing land for cultivation before its watering if it is accustomed to watering in such a period as the ijarah contract is upon; and if water comes to irrigate some of it, the lessee has the option: if he wishes he may rescind the entire ijarah, and if he wishes he may not rescind it and he owes rent in proportion to what was irrigated. And in al-Qunyah: If he leases it and cannot cultivate it immediately due to need for irrigation or digging canals or waiting for water, then if it is such that cultivation is possible within the contract period, it is permissible, otherwise not, as if he leases it in winter for nine months and it cannot be planted in winter, it is permissible because it is possible within the period; but if benefit is entirely impossible, like saline land, the ijarah is invalid. And in the issue of leasing in winter, the rent is for the entire period, not only for what is benefitted; and it is said: for what is benefitted. And know that leasing land is not limited to cultivation, for building and planting trees, as the matns might suggest; indeed al-Hidayah states that land is leased for cultivation and other things. And Ghayat al-Bayan said: By other than cultivation he meant building, planting trees, making bricks and pottery, and similar uses of the land. Thus when you know that, the validity of ijarah contracts in our time becomes clear: that land is leased for resting and grazing, intending thereby to obligate rent simply by being able to use it absolutely, whether water covers it and cultivation is possible or not; there is no doubt of its validity because he did not lease it specifically for cultivation so that lack of water would rescind it. And in al-Walwaljiyah: He leased land to make bricks in it; the ijarah is invalid. Then it is two ways: if the soil has value, he guarantees its value and the bricks are his; if it has no value, nothing is upon him, the bricks are his, and he guarantees any damage to the land if it is damaged. And in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidayah: Leasing land occupied by someone else's crop: if the crop is lawfully there, e.g., via ijarah, it is not permissible to lease it until the crop is harvested, unless the lease is made future; if the crop is without legal basis, the ijarah is valid because the crop must be uprooted, and the lessor in this case is able to deliver what he leased by compelling the crop owner to uproot it whether it is ripe or not, because the owner has no right to keep it. A house occupied by the belongings of a resident who is not a lessee: its ijarah is valid, and the term starts from the time it is delivered empty; likewise in al-Khulasa: if he leased the cultivated land and then delivered it after the crop was harvested and threshed, the ijarah becomes valid. If the lessee says 'I leased the land from you while it was empty' and the lessor says 'No, it was occupied by my crop,' the situation is judged accordingly; likewise in al-Muntaqa. And in Fatawa al-Fadli: The word is that of the lessor.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn about specifying the crop in land ijarah. It begins by affirming that specifying what is to be planted is required due to practical consensus (ijma' 'amali) to prevent dispute. If the lessee is given free choice, the contract is valid. If not specified, the contract is initially invalid but becomes valid once planting occurs, and the full rent is due. The commentary draws analogies (qiyas) with hiring a garment or a cooking pot. Incidental benefits like water and path are included by default. It then provides numerous subsidiary rulings: In a one-year lease with free choice, two crops (spring and autumn) may be planted. If land is leased before its usual watering time, it is valid if watering is expected. If only part of the land gets water, the lessee may cancel the whole contract or pay rent proportionally. If immediate cultivation is impossible but possible within the term, the contract is valid. If completely impossible (e.g., saline land), the contract is invalid. In winter leases, rent covers the full period. The passage emphasizes that land can be leased for building, planting trees, making bricks, etc., not just cultivation. Modern practices of leasing for grazing or resting are valid if not specifically tied to cultivation. It also discusses leasing land occupied by another's crop, and houses occupied by belongings, providing rules for validity.

Key Terms
الإجماع العملي (al-ijma' al-'amali): Practical consensus of the Muslims, used as a proof for the necessity of specifying the crop.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about a term of the contract, which renders the ijarah invalid unless resolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone leases land for one year with the condition 'you may plant whatever you wish', how many crops can the lessee plant according to al-Qunyah?
A) One crop only
B) Two crops: spring and autumn
C) As many as he can within the year
D) Only the crop specified at contract

Key Takeaway
Crop specification in land ijarah is essential to avoid dispute; without it, the contract becomes valid upon planting, and the land can be used for various purposes beyond cultivation.

Leasing Land for Building and Planting: The Hanafi Principle
States the permissibility of leasing land for building and planting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that leasing land for building or planting trees is valid and explain the basis in the school.

Core Idea
Leasing land for building or planting is valid because these are legitimate benefits sought from land.

The Hanafi school considers leasing land for purposes beyond mere cultivation—such as construction and tree planting—as a perfectly valid contract. This lesson establishes the general principle from the commentary on the matn, noting the linguistic point about the word 'ghars' and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that leasing land for building (al-bina') and planting (al-ghars) is valid (sahih). Identify these two purposes as the subject of the ruling.
The ruling is explicit: the contract is sahih, not merely permissible.
2
Note the linguistic note on 'ghars'
The commentator mentions that 'ghars' (planting) can be pronounced with a fat-ha on the ghayn (ghars) or with kasra (ghirs), both meaning what is planted. Recognise this as a minor lexical refinement.
This linguistic detail does not affect the ruling.
3
Understand the legal basis
The reason given is that building and planting are benefits (manafi') sought from land. In Hanafi ijarah, any permissible benefit that is known and deliverable can be the subject of a lease.
This ties the ruling to the general theory of ijarah.
4
Recognise the cross-madhhab dimension
The pre-populated toolbox notes that some schools restrict land ijarah to agricultural use. The Hanafi position is therefore mukhtalaf fih (disputed), but the relied-upon view is validity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different views of what constitutes a benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللبناء والغرس أي وصح استئجار الأرض للبناء والغرس وهو يفتح الغين بمعنى المغروس وقد جاء فيه الكسر ؛ كذا في المغرب لأنها منفعة تقصد بالأراضي. وفي القنية : ولا يجوز لمستأجر السبيل أن يبنى فيه غرفة لنفسه إلا أن يزيد في الأجرة ولا يضر بالبناء وإن كان معطلاً غالباً ولا يرغب المستأجر إلا على هذا الوجه جاز من غير زيادة في الأجرة إذا قال القيم أو المالك لمستأجرها أذنت لك في عمارتها فعمرها بإذنه يرجع على القيم والمالك، وهذا إذا يرجع معظم منفعته إلى المالك، أما إذا رجع إلى المستأجر وفيه ضرر بالدار كالبالوعة أو شغل بعضها كالتنور فلا ما لم يشترط الرجوع ذكره في الوقف
His statement: (And for building and planting) i.e., it is valid to lease land for building and planting, and it is pronounced with fatha on the ghayn meaning what is planted, and it has also come with kasra; likewise in al-Mughrib because it is a benefit sought from lands. And in al-Qunyah: It is not permissible for the lessee of a 'sabeel' to build a room for himself in it unless he increases the rent and does not harm the building; and if it is often idle and the lessee does not desire except in this manner, it is permissible without increase in rent. If the overseer (qayyim) or owner says to its lessee: 'I give you permission to repair it' and he repairs it with his permission, he may resort to the overseer and the owner. This is if most of its benefit reverts to the owner; but if it reverts to the lessee and there is harm to the house like a drain or occupying some part like an oven, then [it is not permissible] unless he stipulates recourse; this was mentioned in the chapter on waqf.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn statement that leasing land for building and planting is valid. The word 'ghars' (planting) can be pronounced with a fat-ha on the ghayn. The reason is that building and planting are benefits sought from land. It then includes a ruling from al-Qunyah: a lessee of a public waqf (sabeel) cannot build a private room without increasing rent, unless the building does not harm and the lessee has little desire otherwise. If the overseer or owner gives permission for repairs, the lessee can claim the cost from them if most benefit goes to the owner. If most benefit goes to the lessee and there is harm to the premises, it is not permissible unless the recourse condition is stipulated.

Key Terms
غرس (ghars): Planting trees; the act of setting plants in the ground.
استئجار (isti'jar): Leasing; hiring; the contract of ijarah.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit; utility; the subject matter of ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on leasing land for building a house?
A) Valid (sahih)
B) Invalid (batil)
C) Permissible (ja'iz) but disliked
D) Valid only if the builder is the owner

Key Takeaway
Leasing land for construction or tree planting is a valid contract in the Hanafi school, grounded in the general permissibility of beneficial land use.

Special Ruling for Public Waqf (Sabeel): Building and Repairs
Expands on the general principle with specific rulings for public waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a lessee of a public waqf (sabeel) may build or repair, and determine when repair costs can be recovered.

Core Idea
A lessee of a public waqf cannot build a private room without increasing rent, unless minimal harm and lack of desire apply; repairs permitted with recourse if benefit to owner.

The commentary from al-Qunyah provides detailed exceptions for waqf property. This lesson examines the nuanced rules governing a lessee of a 'sabeel' (public waqf) who wishes to build or make repairs. The key is balancing the lessee's interest against the waqf's integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The default rule: a lessee of a public waqf (sabeel) is not allowed to build a room for himself inside the waqf property.
This is because waqf property is for public benefit; private construction would appropriate it.
2
Apply the exceptions
The prohibition is lifted if either (a) the lessee increases the rent and does not harm the building, or (b) the property is often idle and the lessee has little desire for it—then it is permissible even without rent increase.
Both exceptions aim to prevent loss to the waqf while allowing beneficial use.
3
Understand repair permission and recourse
If the overseer (qayyim) or owner gives permission to repair, and the lessee does so, he can reclaim the cost from them. This is conditional on the majority of the benefit reverting to the owner.
If most benefit goes to the lessee, and there is harm (e.g., a drain or oven), no recourse unless stipulated.
4
Distinguish based on benefit and harm
When most benefit returns to the owner, recourse is allowed. When benefit goes to the lessee and causes harm, it is not allowed, unless the condition of recourse was agreed upon.
This prevents the lessee from imposing costs on the waqf for his own benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللبناء والغرس أي وصح استئجار الأرض للبناء والغرس وهو يفتح الغين بمعنى المغروس وقد جاء فيه الكسر ؛ كذا في المغرب لأنها منفعة تقصد بالأراضي. وفي القنية : ولا يجوز لمستأجر السبيل أن يبنى فيه غرفة لنفسه إلا أن يزيد في الأجرة ولا يضر بالبناء وإن كان معطلاً غالباً ولا يرغب المستأجر إلا على هذا الوجه جاز من غير زيادة في الأجرة إذا قال القيم أو المالك لمستأجرها أذنت لك في عمارتها فعمرها بإذنه يرجع على القيم والمالك، وهذا إذا يرجع معظم منفعته إلى المالك، أما إذا رجع إلى المستأجر وفيه ضرر بالدار كالبالوعة أو شغل بعضها كالتنور فلا ما لم يشترط الرجوع ذكره في الوقف
His statement: (And for building and planting) i.e., it is valid to lease land for building and planting, and it is pronounced with fatha on the ghayn meaning what is planted, and it has also come with kasra; likewise in al-Mughrib because it is a benefit sought from lands. And in al-Qunyah: It is not permissible for the lessee of a 'sabeel' to build a room for himself in it unless he increases the rent and does not harm the building; and if it is often idle and the lessee does not desire except in this manner, it is permissible without increase in rent. If the overseer (qayyim) or owner says to its lessee: 'I give you permission to repair it' and he repairs it with his permission, he may resort to the overseer and the owner. This is if most of its benefit reverts to the owner; but if it reverts to the lessee and there is harm to the house like a drain or occupying some part like an oven, then [it is not permissible] unless he stipulates recourse; this was mentioned in the chapter on waqf.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn statement that leasing land for building and planting is valid. The word 'ghars' (planting) can be pronounced with a fat-ha on the ghayn. The reason is that building and planting are benefits sought from land. It then includes a ruling from al-Qunyah: a lessee of a public waqf (sabeel) cannot build a private room without increasing rent, unless the building does not harm and the lessee has little desire otherwise. If the overseer or owner gives permission for repairs, the lessee can claim the cost from them if most benefit goes to the owner. If most benefit goes to the lessee and there is harm to the premises, it is not permissible unless the recourse condition is stipulated.

Key Terms
سبيل (sabeel): Public waqf; property dedicated for charitable use.
قيم (qayyim): Overseer; trustee of a waqf.
رجوع (ruju'): Recourse; the right to claim reimbursement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition can a lessee of a public waqf build a room without increasing rent?
A) If the lessee is poor
B) If the property is often idle and the lessee has little desire for it otherwise
C) If the overseer gives verbal permission
D) It is never allowed without rent increase

Key Takeaway
Building on a public waqf by a lessee is heavily restricted; exceptions exist only for idle property or with rent increase, and repair cost recovery is conditional on benefit to the waqf.
