Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Liability for Beating and Checking Hired Animals: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining liability for beating/checking hired animals and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability for beating/checking a hired animal, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Customary acts are implicitly permitted in a contract; thus, gentle checking of a hired animal does not incur liability.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a crucial question in Ijarah: if a hirer beats or checks a hired animal and it dies, is he liable? The Hanafi school split on this issue, with Abu Hanifa initially holding strict liability, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued that customary acts are covered by the contract's general permission. The passage notes that Abu Hanifa later retracted to their position, establishing the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is beating (darb) or checking (kabh) a hired animal. The ruling is whether the hirer is liable (yadman) if the animal perishes. The passage presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
The dispute is about the scope of permission in the hire contract.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa held that the hirer guarantees the animal if he beats or checks it, even if the act is customary. His reasoning: The permission is conditional upon safety (mujawwaz bi shart al-salama). Any beating or checking increases risk and constitutes transgression (ta'di).
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that the hirer does not guarantee if the act is customary (fi'l mut'araf). Their reasoning: Customary acts are implicitly permitted by the contract (al-mut'araf yadkhul taht al-mutlaq). Since these acts are expected, they fall under the general permission, so no liability.
The key term is 'mut'araf' (customary).
4
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: if a hirer gently pulls the bridle (kabh) to stop the animal and it dies, according to the Sahibayn there is no liability; according to Abu Hanifa's original view, there is liability.
The hirer would owe compensation in the latter case.
5
Identify the Tarjih (Mufta Bihi)
The passage states in Ghayat al-Bayan from al-Tatimma that the correct view is that Abu Hanifa retracted to the position of the Sahibayn. Therefore, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view is no liability for customary acts.
This is an example of a later revision within the school.

Source Text

قوله: (وبالضرب والكبح أي يضمن بهما إذا هلكت وفي المغرب : كبح الدابة باللجام إذا ردها وهو أن يجذبها إلى نفسه لتقف ولا تجري وقالا لا يضمن إذا فعل فعلاً متعارفاً لأن المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد فكان حاصلاً بإذنه فلا يضمنه، لأبي حنيفة قوله : (وإن حملاه معاً وجب النصف على المستأجر) نقل بعده في المنح عن الخلاصة أنه يضمن القيمة لأن النصف مأذون فيه والنصف الآخر بغير إذن وبحمله يضمن نصف هذا النصف . ربع ونقله الشرنبلالي عن تتمة الفتاوى . قال بعض الفضلاء ونقله في حاشية الشلبي على الزيلعي عنهما أيضاً وفي حاشية سرى الدين عن الخلاصة والمبسوط .اهـ. قلت ومثله في التتارخانية عن الذخيرة فليراجع المحيط فلعل ما هنا محرف أو المراد نصف الزائد يؤيده ما في البزازية : وأن يحمل عشرة فجعل عشرين وحملا معاً ضمن ربع القيمة لأن النصف مأذون والنصف لا فينتصف هذا النصف ومثله ما مر عن الخلاصة قوله : (وقيده) أي كلام المتن قوله : (إذا هلك) أي إذا هلك الحيوان المستأجر . أن الإذن مقيد بشرط السلامة إذ يتحقق السوق بدونه وإنما هما للمبالغة فيتقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق. قيد بالضرب والكبح لأنه لا يضمن بالسوق اتفاقاً، وظاهر ما في الهداية أن للمستأجر الضرب ولا إثم عليه للإذن العرفي فيه وإن كان مقيداً بشرط السلامة وفي غاية البيان إن ضربه للدابة يكون تعدياً موجباً للضمان بخلاف العبد المستأجر فإنه ليس له ضربه ويضمن به اتفاقاً لأنه يؤمر وينهي لفهمه فلا ضرورة إلى الضرب. وللسيد ضرب عبده تأديباً وللأب والوصي ضرب الصغير للتأديب لكن مقيد عند أبي حنيفة بشرط السلامة حتى يضمنان لو هلك بضربهما لأن التأديب قد يقع بالزجر والتعريك. وفي غاية البيان عن التتمة : الأصح أن أبا حنيفة رجع إلى قولهما، والمعلم والأستاذ ليس لهما ضرب الصغير إلا بإذن الأب أو الوصي فإن مات لا ضمان عليهما إذا كان بإذن وإلا ضمنا. وأما ضربه دابة نفسه فقال في القنية : وعند أبي حنيفة لا يضربها أصلاً ولو كانت ملكه، وكذا حكم كل ما يستعمل من الحيوانات ثم قال : لا يخاصم ضارب الحيوان فيما يحتاج إليه للتأديب وبخاصم فيما زاد عليه ولا يجوز ضرب أختها الصغيرة التي ليس لها ولي بترك الصلوات إذا بلغت عشراً ثم قال له أن يضرب اليتيم فيما يضرب ولده به وردت الأخبار والآثار. وفي الروضة له أن يكره ولده الصغير على تعليم القرآن والأدب والعلم لأن ذلك فرض على الوالدين، ولو أمر غيره بضرب عبده حل للمأمور ضرب عبده بخلاف الحر قال رضي الله عنه : فهذا تنصيص على عدم جواز ضرب ولد الآمر بأمره بخلاف المعلم لأن المأمور بضربه نيابة عن الأب لمصلحته والمعلم يضربه بحكم الملك بتمليك أبيه لمصلحة العلم. وأما ضرب الزوجة فجائز في مواضع أربعة وما في معناها على ترك الزينة لزوجها وهو يريدها، وترك الإجابة إلى الفراش، وترك الغسل، والخروج من المنزل. وفي ضرب امرأته وولده على ترك الصلاة روايتان كذا قالوا ومما في معناها ما إذا ضربت جارية زوجها غيرة ولا تتعظ بوعظه فله ضربها ؛ كذا في القنية. ويلحق به ما إذا ضربت الولد الذي لا يعقل عند بكائه لأن ضرب الدابة إذا كان ممنوعاً فهذا أولى ومنه ما إذا شتمته أو مزقت ثيابه أو أخذت لحيته أو قالت له يا حمار يا أبله أو لعنته سواء شتمها أو لا على قول العامة . إذا شتمت أجنبياً. ومنه ما إذا كشفت وجهها لغير محرم أو كلمت أجنبياً أو تكلمت عامداً مع الزوج أو شاغبت معه ليسمع صوتها الأجنبي. ومنه ما إذا أعطت من بيته شيئاً من الطعام بلا إذنه إن كانت العادة لم تجر به وإن كانت العادة مسامحة المرأة بذلك بلا مشورة الزوج فليس ومنه ما فجعل عشرين وحملا معاً ضمن ربع القيمة لأن النصف مأذون والنصف لا فينتصف هذا النصف ومثله ما مر عن الخلاصة قوله : (وقيده) أي كلام المتن قوله : (إذا هلك) أي إذا هلك الحيوان المستأجر
His statement: (And by beating and checking) i.e., he guarantees by them if it perishes. And in al-Mughrib: 'Kabh' of the animal by the bridle when he pulls it back, meaning he pulls it towards himself to stop and not run. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not guarantee if he does a customary act, because the customary is included under the absolute contract, so it occurred with his permission, thus he does not guarantee it. For Abu Hanifa [the position is that he guarantees]. His statement: (And if they both loaded together, half is obligatory on the hirer) It is transmitted after it in al-Minh from al-Khulasah that he guarantees the value because half is permitted and the other half without permission, and by his loading he guarantees half of this half: a quarter. And al-Shurunbulali transmitted it from Tatimmat al-Fatawa. Some virtuous one said, and it was transmitted in Hashiyat al-Shalabi ala al-Zaylai from both of them, and in Hashiyat Sirr al-Din from al-Khulasah and al-Mabsut. End. I say: and the like is in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Dhakhirah, so let one refer to al-Muhit; perhaps what is here is corrupted or the intended meaning is half of the excess, corroborated by what is in al-Bazzaziyyah: and that he loads ten, then he made it twenty and loaded together, he guarantees a quarter of the value because half is permitted and half is not, so this half is halved. And the like is what passed from al-Khulasah. His statement: (and he conditioned it) i.e., the words of the matn. His statement: (if it perishes) i.e., if the hired animal perishes. That permission is conditioned upon safety, since driving is realized without it, and they (beating and checking) are for exaggeration, so it is conditioned by the quality of safety, like passing through a road. It is restricted to beating and checking because he does not guarantee by driving unanimously. And what appears in al-Hidayah is that the hirer may beat and there is no sin on him due to customary permission, even if it is conditioned upon safety. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: If he beats the animal it is transgression leading to liability, unlike the hired slave, for he has no right to beat him and he guarantees by it unanimously because he (the slave) can be commanded and prohibited due to his understanding, so there is no need for beating. And the master may beat his slave for discipline, and the father and guardian may beat the child for discipline, but it is conditioned according to Abu Hanifa by safety, so they guarantee if he dies from their beating, because discipline can be achieved by scolding and rubbing. And in Ghayat al-Bayan from al-Tatimma: The correct view is that Abu Hanifa retracted to their position (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And the teacher and instructor have no right to beat the child except with permission of the father or guardian; if the child dies, there is no liability on them if with permission, otherwise they guarantee. As for beating one's own animal, he said in al-Qunyah: According to Abu Hanifa, he may not beat it at all, even if it is his property, and similarly the ruling for every animal used. Then he said: One who beats an animal is not disputed regarding what is needed for discipline, but is disputed regarding what exceeds that. And it is not permissible to beat his little sister who has no guardian for neglecting prayers when she reaches ten years. Then he said: He may beat the orphan in the same way he beats his own child, as reported in hadith and traditions. And in al-Rawdah: He may compel his young child to learn Quran, good manners, and knowledge because that is an obligation upon the parents. And if he orders someone else to beat his slave, it is permissible for the commanded one to beat his slave, unlike a free person. He (Radi Allahu Anhu) said: This is a specification that it is not permissible to beat the child of the one commanding by his order, unlike the teacher, because the commanded one beats as a deputy of the father for his benefit, while the teacher beats by virtue of ownership due to the father's transfer for the benefit of knowledge. As for beating the wife, it is permissible in four situations and what is similar to them: leaving adornment for her husband when he desires it, leaving answering the call to bed, leaving ghusl (ritual bath), and leaving the house. Regarding beating his wife and child for leaving prayer, there are two narrations. That is what they said. And among what is similar to it is when she beats the female slave of her husband out of jealousy and is not deterred by his admonition, so he may beat her; this is in al-Qunyah. And annexed to it is when she beats the child who does not understand when he cries, because if beating an animal is prohibited, this is even more so. And among it is when she curses him, tears his clothes, grabs his beard, or says to him 'O donkey, O idiot,' or curses him, whether she curses him or not according to the common people. If she curses a stranger. And among it is when she uncovers her face in front of a non-mahram, or talks to a non-mahram, or deliberately speaks loudly with the husband so that a non-mahram hears her voice. And among it is when she gives something from his house of food without his permission if it is not customary; if it is customary for the woman to be lenient in that without consulting the husband, then it is not [actionable]. And among it is what he made twenty and loaded together, he guarantees a quarter of the value because half is permitted and half is not, so this half is halved, and the like is what passed from al-Khulasah. His statement: (and he conditioned it) i.e., the words of the matn. His statement: (if it perishes) i.e., if the hired animal perishes.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This lengthy passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq covers multiple rulings on beating and hitting in the context of Ijarah and beyond. It begins with an inter-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding liability for beating or checking a hired animal. The Sahibayn hold that if the act is customary (like a gentle pull to stop), there is no liability because such acts are implicitly permitted by the contract. Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that any beating or checking that causes death incurs liability, because the permission is conditional upon safety. Later, the passage notes that Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of the Sahibayn (according to some sources). The passage then expands to cover: hitting a hired slave (not allowed, and if done, liability), master hitting his own slave (permissible for discipline but conditional on safety), father/guardian hitting a child (permissible for discipline but conditional on safety; Abu Hanifa later agreed with the Sahibayn), teacher hitting a student (only with father's permission), hitting one's own animal (not allowed at all according to Abu Hanifa), and hitting a wife (permissible in four specific cases related to marital obligations). The passage also includes numerous details about what constitutes permissible hitting of a wife, citing examples from al-Qunyah. Finally, it returns to the earlier discussion about the hired animal, clarifying that the permission for beating and checking is qualified by the condition of safety. The overall lesson is that in Hanafi law, the general principle is that hitting animals or humans is only permissible when necessity or custom dictates, and even then, liability arises if safety is compromised.

Key Terms
الضرب (al-darb): Striking an animal or human as a means of control or discipline.
الكبح (al-kabh): Pulling the bridle to stop or check an animal.
التعدي (al-ta'di): Transgression or overstepping the bounds of permission, leading to liability.
متعارف (mut'araf): Customary, conventionally practiced.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling if a hirer gently pulls the bridle (kabh) of a hired horse to stop it, and the horse dies from an unrelated cause?
A) The hirer must pay full compensation because he touched the horse.
B) The hirer is liable because any action besides riding is prohibited.
C) The hirer is not liable because the action was customary and implicitly permitted.
D) The hirer is liable only if he intended to harm the horse.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, customary actions in a hire contract are implicitly permitted, so liability for beating/checking arises only when the act exceeds custom.

Liability for Changing Saddle or Load on a Hired Animal
Explaining liability for changing saddle/load on hired animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hirer changes the saddle or load on a hired animal to a different genus, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Changing to a different genus of saddle or load makes the hirer liable for the animal's full value.

Hiring an animal comes with conditions. If the hirer alters the specified saddle or load, the legal consequences depend on whether the new item is of the same genus and custom. This lesson unpacks a classical Hanafi ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, revealing a nuanced dispute and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act that triggers liability? The hirer changes the saddle to a type not normally used, or puts a pack-saddle on an animal hired for riding. The ruling: if the animal perishes, the hirer is liable for the full value.
The act of changing to a different genus is the key.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas: just as substituting iron for wheat in a sale makes the buyer liable for the whole, here changing the saddle type is like not taking delivery of the specified item.
Analogy to a sale where the commodity is changed.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the new saddle is for a different purpose (e.g., carrying loads vs. riding), so the hirer has not utilized the contracted service at all. This change is to a different genus, making the original contract unfulfilled.
The illa is identified as change of genus.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that even if the pack-saddle is of the same type (commonly used), liability arises. The Sahibayn say no liability if it is the usual type. Later scholars added distinctions based on travel and social status.
The dispute is about whether custom can affect the genus classification.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq supports the absolute liability view from al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which is zahir al-riwaya. This is the mufta bihi position.
Zahir al-riwaya takes precedence over later detailed distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ونزع السرج والإكاف والإسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله) يعني لو اكترى حماراً بسرج فنزع السرج فأسرجه سرجاً لا يسرج بمثله الحمر أو أوكفه مطلقاً أو نزع الإكاف لا يسرج بمثله فعطب ضمن جميع قيمته لأن الإكاف يستعمل لغير ما يستعمل له السرج وهو الحمل وأثره يخالف أيضاً لأنه لا ينبسط انبساط السرج فكان في حق الدابة خلافاً إلى جنس غير المسمى فلم يصر مستوفياً شيئاً من المسمى فيضمن الكل كما لو أبدل الحديد مكان الحنطة. وقيد بكونه لا يسرج بمثله لأنه إذا استأجرها بإكاف فأوكفها بإكاف مثله أو أسرجها مكان الإكاف لا يضمن ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وإنما قلنا في الإكاف مطلقاً لأن المنقول في الخلاصة أيضاً أنه لو استأجرها بسرج فأوكفها بإكاف يوكف مثلها فهلكت ضمن كل القيمة عند أبي حنيفة وفيها أيضاً لو استأجرها عريانة فأسرجها وركبها ضمن قال مشايخنا : إن استأجرها من بلد إلى بلد لا يضمن وإن استأجرها ليركبها في المصر إن كان المستكري من الأشراف لا يضمن وإن كان من العوام الذين يركبون عرياناً ضمن، ولو تكارى دابة ولم يذكر السرج والإكاف وسلمها عريانة فركبها بهذا أو بهذا إن كان مثله يركب بسرج يضمن إذا ركبها بإكاف، وإن كان يركب بكل واحد منهما لا يضمن إذا ركبها بهذا أو بهذا قال تأويله إذا ركب من بلد إلى بلد ا هـ . واعلم أن المنقول في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد الضمان مطلقاً من غير تفصيل المشايخ فكان هو المذهب لأنه ظاهر الرواية كما لا يخفى. في شرح الجامع الصغير أنه يضمن جميع القيمة لأنه ذكر الضمان مطلقاً فينصرف إلى الكل لأنه خلافه صورة ومعنى. وقال في غاية البيان قلت: ينبغي أن يكون الأصح ضمان قدر الزيادة وفي الخلاصة : ولو استأجرها بغير لجام فألجمها لا يضمن إلا إذا ألجم بلجام لا يلجم مثلها ا هـ. وقوله : (أو نزع الإكاف فأسرجه بما لا يسرج مثله) قال الرملي قال في السراج الوهاج : ولو اكترى حماراً بإكاف فأسرجه ونزع الإكاف فلا ضمان عليه لأن ضرر السرج أقل من ضرر الإكاف، وينبغي حمله على ما إذا أسرجه بسرج يسرج بمثله الحمر، أما إذا كان لا يسرج بمثله الحمر فإنه يضمن كما هنا فلا مخالفة بينهما فتأمل قوله : (وكذا إذا أبدله لأن الحمار الخ) أي وكذا لا يضمن . وعبارة غاية البيان وقال الكرخي في مختصره : إن لم يكن عليه لجام فألجمه فلا ضمان عليه إذا كان مثله يلجم بذلك اللجام ، وكذلك إن أبد له وذلك لأن الحمار لا يختلف باللجام وغيره ولا يتلف به فلم يضمن بالجامه والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وهو الموفق والمعين قال أستاذنا مؤلف هذه الحواشي
His statement: (And removing the saddle and pad, and saddling with something that is not used to saddle its like) means: If he hires a donkey with a saddle, then removes the saddle and puts on a saddle that donkeys are not normally saddled with, or puts a pad on it absolutely, or removes the pad and puts something that is not used to pad its like, and it perishes, he is liable for the entire value, because the pad is used for something other than what the saddle is used for, namely carrying loads, and its effect is also different because it does not spread out like the saddle. So it is, in respect of the animal, a change to a different genus than what was specified, so he is not considered to have taken delivery of anything from what was specified, so he is liable for the whole, just as if he substituted iron for wheat. And it is qualified by 'not saddling its like' because if he hires it with a pad and puts on a pad like it, or puts a saddle in place of the pad, he is not liable; so in al-Khulasa. And we said 'absolutely' regarding the pad because what is transmitted in al-Khulasa is that if he hires it with a saddle and puts a pad on it that is like its pads, and it perishes, he is liable for the entire value according to Abu Hanifa. And in it also: if he hires it bare and saddles it and rides it, he is liable. Our scholars said: If he hires it from one town to another, he is not liable; and if he hires it to ride in the city, if the hirer is of the nobles, he is not liable; but if he is of the common people who ride bare, he is liable. If he hires an animal without mentioning saddle and pad, and he delivers it bare, and he rides it with this or that: if someone like him rides with a saddle, he is liable if he rides it with a pad; and if he rides with each of them, he is not liable if he rides it with this or that. He said its interpretation is when he rides from one town to another. And know that what is transmitted in al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is liability absolutely without the detail of our scholars, and that is the madhhab because it is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). In Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, that he is liable for the entire value because he mentioned liability absolutely, so it refers to the whole because it is contrary in form and meaning. And it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: I say: it should be that the more correct is liability for the amount of the increase. And in al-Khulasa: If he hires it without a bridle and puts a bridle on it, he is not liable unless he puts a bridle that is not like what is normally used for its like. And his statement: (Or if he removes the pad and saddles it with something that is not used to saddle its like) – al-Ramli said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he hires a donkey with a pad and saddles it and removes the pad, there is no liability because the harm of the saddle is less than the harm of the pad. And it should be interpreted as when he saddles it with a saddle that is used to saddle donkeys; but if it is not used to saddle donkeys, then he is liable as here, so there is no conflict between them. His statement: (And likewise if he substitutes it because the donkey, etc.) meaning likewise he is not liable. And the expression of Ghayat al-Bayan: And al-Karkhi said in his Mukhtasar: If there was no bridle on it and he puts a bridle on it, there is no liability if his like is bridled with that bridle; and likewise if he substituted it, because the donkey does not differ with the bridle and without it, and it is not harmed by it. And Allah knows best; He is the Grantor of success and the Helper. Our teacher, the author of these glosses, said.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on a specific ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the liability of a hirer who changes the type of saddle or load on a hired animal. The passage type is a ruling with proof, using analogy (qiyas) and references to authoritative texts like al-Khulasa and al-Kafi. The core ruling: If a person hires a donkey with a saddle and then removes it and puts on a different type of saddle not normally used for that animal, or puts a pack-saddle (ikaf) instead, and the animal perishes, the hirer is liable for the full value. The reason is that the pack-saddle is used for carrying loads, not riding, and its effect is different; this is a change to a different genus of use, so the hirer is not considered to have utilized the specified item at all, analogous to substituting iron for wheat in a contract. However, if the new saddle is of the same type that is normally used, there is no liability. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that changing to a pack-saddle even if it is of the same type (i.e., a pack-saddle of the kind usually used) still incurs full liability, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differentiate. Later scholars (mashayikh) introduced further distinctions based on the nature of travel and social status: if hired for a long journey, no liability; if for local riding, nobles are not liable but commoners are. The author then notes that the relied-upon position (madhhab) is the absolute liability from al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Some later authorities suggest liability for the increase in value only. The passage also addresses the addition of a bridle (lijam): no liability if it is of the type normally used. The commentary by al-Ramli harmonizes different texts: if a saddle is less harmful than a pack-saddle, then no liability when switching from pack-saddle to saddle of the usual type.

Key Terms
سرج (saraj): Saddle for riding an animal.
إكاف (ikaf): Pack-saddle or load-bearing saddle used for carrying goods.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
لجام (lijam): Bridle, bit for controlling the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person hires a donkey with a saddle and then replaces it with a pack-saddle (ikaf) that is normally used for that animal, what is the liability if the donkey perishes?
A) Full liability according to all Hanafi scholars.
B) No liability according to Sahibayn, but full liability according to Abu Hanifa.
C) No liability in all cases because the pack-saddle is less harmful.
D) Only partial liability for the increase in value.

Key Takeaway
Changing a hired animal's saddle to a different genus (e.g., from riding to pack-saddle) makes the hirer liable for full value if the animal perishes; the relied-upon Hanafi view is absolute liability regardless of custom.

Full Liability for Changing Saddle to Packsaddle: Change of Genus
Core ruling on liability for changing saddle to packsaddle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that changing a saddle to a packsaddle on a hired donkey incurs full liability if the animal perishes, and apply the qiyas to change of genus.

Core Idea
Changing saddle to packsaddle is a change of genus, triggering full liability if the animal dies.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hirer removes the saddle from a hired donkey and replaces it with a packsaddle, or vice versa. The key principle is that the saddle (sarj) and packsaddle (ikaf) are considered different genera (jins) because they serve different purposes—riding vs. carrying loads. Changing them is analogous to replacing wheat with iron in a contract, which incurs full compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the equipment
The hirer removes the saddle (sarj) from the hired donkey and puts a packsaddle (ikaf), or removes the packsaddle and puts a saddle. Note that the animal perishes as a result.
The ruling applies only if the new equipment is not similar to the original in kind and custom.
2
Determine the genus of each item
The saddle (sarj) is designed for riding; the packsaddle (ikaf) is designed for carrying loads. They have different shapes and effects on the animal. In Hanafi fiqh, they are considered different genera (jins).
Even if the packsaddle is of a size used for that donkey, it remains a different genus.
3
Apply the qiyas to change of genus
The situation is analogized to a contract where wheat is replaced with iron—a clear change of genus. Just as that change incurs full compensation, so does changing the equipment on the donkey.
The illa (effective cause) is the change of genus (jins ghayr al-musamma).
4
State the ruling
The hirer is liable for the full value of the donkey (daman al-kull) because he caused the loss by using equipment of a different genus, which is not customarily used and harms the animal.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها السرج والإكاف أو الإسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله وسلوك طريق غير ما عينه وتفاوتاً له ضربها. ومنه ما إذا ادعت عليه وليس منه ما إذا طلبت نفقتها أو كسوتها وألحت لأن لصاحب الحق يد الملازمة ولسان التقاضي؛ كذا في البزازية من النوع الثالث في الضرب من الاختيار. وأسرجه بسرج قوله: (ونزع السرج والإكاف والإسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله) يعني لو اكترى حماراً بسرج فنزع السرج فأسرجه سرجاً لا يسرج بمثله الحمر أو أوكفه مطلقاً أو نزع الإكاف لا يسرج بمثله فعطب ضمن جميع قيمته لأن الإكاف يستعمل لغير ما يستعمل له السرج وهو الحمل وأثره يخالف أيضاً لأنه لا ينبسط انبساط استأجرها عريانة فأسرجها وركبها ضمن قال مشايخنا: إن استأجرها من بلد إلى بلد لا يضمن وإن استأجرها ليركبها في المصر إن كان المستكري من الأشراف لا يضمن وإن كان من العوام الذين يركبون عرياناً ضمن، ولو تكارى دابة ولم يذكر السرج والإكاف وسلمها عريانة فركبها بهذا أو بهذا إن كان مثله يركب بسرج يضمن إذا ركبها بإكاف، وإن كان يركب بكل واحد منهما لا يضمن إذا ركبها بهذا أو بهذا قال تأويله إذا ركب من بلد إلى بلد ا هـ . واعلم أن المنقول في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد الضمان مطلقاً من غير تفصيل المشايخ فكان هو المذهب لأنه ظاهر الرواية كما لا يخفى. في شرح الجامع الصغير أنه يضمن جميع القيمة لأنه ذكر الضمان مطلقاً فينصرف إلى الكل لأنه خلافه صورة ومعنى. وقال في غاية البيان قلت: ينبغي أن يكون الأصح ضمان قدر الزيادة وفي الخلاصة: ولو استأجرها بغير لجام فألجمها لا يضمن إلا إذا وكذا إذا أبدله لأن الحمار لا يختلف وكذا لا يضمن. وعبارة غاية البيان وقال الكرخي في مختصره: إن لم يكن عليه لجام فألجمه فلا ضمان عليه إذا كان مثله يلجم بذلك اللجام، وكذلك إن أبدله وذلك لأن الحمار لا يختلف باللجام وغيره ولا يتلف به فلم يضمن بالجامه والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وهو الموفق والمعين قال أستاذنا مؤلف هذه الحواشي
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is contrary in it. The saddle and the pack-saddle, or saddling with something not similar, and taking a path other than specified and difference... He said: (And removing the saddle and pack-saddle and saddling with something not similar to it) means if one hires a donkey with a saddle then removes the saddle and saddles it with a saddle not similar to what is usually saddled on donkeys, or puts a packsaddle on it absolutely, or removes the packsaddle and saddles with something not similar, and it perishes, he is liable for its full value...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by commentary. The author discusses the scenario where a hirer of a donkey changes the equipment (saddle or packsaddle) to something not similar or of a different kind. The key principle: if the new equipment is of a different genus (jins) and not customarily used for the animal, the hirer becomes liable for full compensation if the animal dies, because he causes a change that is detrimental. The analogy is made to someone who replaces wheat with iron in a contract. If the equipment is similar (like replacing one saddle with another of the same type), there is no liability. There is a partial difference from Shuyukh regarding the place of riding; in long-distance travel, the custom may exempt liability. The relied-upon position (al-madhhab) from al-Kafi is absolute liability because it is the clear transmission (zahir al-riwayah). Later, it is mentioned that if the animal is ridden without any equipment, liability depends on the status of the hirer (noble or commoner). The passage also covers the case of putting a bridle (lujam) — since donkeys are not affected by bridles, there is no liability unless the bridle is of a type not used for such donkeys.

Key Terms
السرج (al-sarj): The saddle placed on a riding animal (particularly a donkey) for seating the rider.
الإكاف (al-ikaf): A packsaddle used for carrying loads, distinct from a riding saddle.
الضمان (al-daman): Financial liability to compensate for loss or damage.
المثل (al-mithl): Similar; in this context, equipment of the same type and customarily used for that animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Full compensation because the saddle and packsaddle are different genera.
B) No compensation because the packsaddle is similar and customary.
C) Compensation only for the difference in value.
D) Half compensation.

Key Takeaway
Changing a saddle to a packsaddle on a hired donkey triggers full liability only if the packsaddle is not similar (mithl) to what is customary; the illa is the change of genus.

Exceptions and Custom: When No Liability Arises for Equipment Changes
Exceptions to liability for equipment changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scenarios where changing equipment on a hired donkey does not incur liability, including similar replacements, custom-based travel, status of hirer, and the bridle case.

Core Idea
No liability if the new equipment is similar, or if custom exempts based on travel or the hirer's status.

While the general rule is liability for changing saddle to packsaddle, the Hanafi school recognizes several exceptions. In this lesson, we explore the cases where no liability arises: when the replacement is similar (mithl), when the hirer is riding in a city and is of noble status, when traveling long distances, or when the change involves a bridle (lujam) that does not harm the animal. These exceptions are derived from the Shuyukh's distinctions and show how custom ('urf) can affect legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception for similar equipment
The first exception is when the new equipment is similar (mithl) to the original and customarily used. For example, replacing a saddle with another saddle of the same type, or a packsaddle with another packsaddle of the same type. In such cases, there is no liability even if the animal dies.
This is based on the condition 'بما لا يسرج بمثله' — the ruling applies only when the new item is not similar.
2
Analyze the custom-based exception for travel and city
When the donkey is hired for long-distance travel (from city to city), changing equipment may not incur liability. In the city, the ruling depends on the hirer's status: noblemen (ashraf) who normally ride with saddles are not liable if they use a packsaddle; commoners ('awam) who usually ride bare are liable.
These distinctions are from the Shuyukh, not the Zahir al-Riwayah, but they are mentioned in the source.
3
Examine the bridle (lujam) case
If a donkey is hired without a bridle and the hirer puts one on, there is no liability because the donkey is not harmed by a bridle. The text says: 'الحمار لا يختلف باللجام وغيره' — the donkey does not differ with or without a bridle.
This exception is based on the principle that no harm is caused.
4
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi) among these exceptions
The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is absolute liability in all cases of changing saddle to packsaddle, ignoring the Shuyukh's distinctions. However, the exceptions for similar equipment and bridles are accepted even in Zahir al-Riwayah. The exceptions for travel and status are considered later refinements and are not universally applied in fatwa.
The student should know both the general rule and the exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها السرج والإكاف أو الإسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله وسلوك طريق غير ما عينه وتفاوتاً له ضربها. ومنه ما إذا ادعت عليه وليس منه ما إذا طلبت نفقتها أو كسوتها وألحت لأن لصاحب الحق يد الملازمة ولسان التقاضي؛ كذا في البزازية من النوع الثالث في الضرب من الاختيار. وأسرجه بسرج قوله: (ونزع السرج والإكاف والإسراج بما لا يسرج بمثله) يعني لو اكترى حماراً بسرج فنزع السرج فأسرجه سرجاً لا يسرج بمثله الحمر أو أوكفه مطلقاً أو نزع الإكاف لا يسرج بمثله فعطب ضمن جميع قيمته لأن الإكاف يستعمل لغير ما يستعمل له السرج وهو الحمل وأثره يخالف أيضاً لأنه لا ينبسط انبساط السرج فكان في حق الدابة خلافاً إلى جنس غير المسمى فلم يصر مستوفياً شيئاً من المسمى فيضمن الكل كما لو أبدل الحديد مكان الحنطة. وقيد بكونه لا يسرج بمثله لأنه إذا استأجرها بإكاف فأوكفها بإكاف مثله أو أسرجها مكان الإكاف لا يضمن؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وإنما قلنا في الإكاف مطلقاً لأن المنقول في الخلاصة أيضاً أنه لو استأجرها بسرج فأوكفها بإكاف يوكف مثلها فهلكت ضمن كل القيمة عند أبي حنيفة وفيها أيضاً لو استأجرها عريانة فأسرجها وركبها ضمن قال مشايخنا: إن استأجرها من بلد إلى بلد لا يضمن وإن استأجرها ليركبها في المصر إن كان المستكري من الأشراف لا يضمن وإن كان من العوام الذين يركبون عرياناً ضمن، ولو تكارى دابة ولم يذكر السرج والإكاف وسلمها عريانة فركبها بهذا أو بهذا إن كان مثله يركب بسرج يضمن إذا ركبها بإكاف، وإن كان يركب بكل واحد منهما لا يضمن إذا ركبها بهذا أو بهذا قال تأويله إذا ركب من بلد إلى بلد ا هـ . واعلم أن المنقول في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد الضمان مطلقاً من غير تفصيل المشايخ فكان هو المذهب لأنه ظاهر الرواية كما لا يخفى. في شرح الجامع الصغير أنه يضمن جميع القيمة لأنه ذكر الضمان مطلقاً فينصرف إلى الكل لأنه خلافه صورة ومعنى. وقال في غاية البيان قلت: ينبغي أن يكون الأصح ضمان قدر الزيادة وفي الخلاصة: ولو استأجرها بغير لجام فألجمها لا يضمن إلا إذا وكذا إذا أبدله لأن الحمار لا يختلف باللجام وغيره؛ كذا وصحح قاضيخان ألجم بلجام لا يلجم مثلها ا هـ. في قوله: (أو نزع الإكاف فأسرجه بما لا يسرج مثله) قال الرملي قال في السراج الوهاج: ولو اكترى حماراً بإكاف فأسرجه ونزع الإكاف فلا ضمان عليه لأن ضرر السرج أقل من ضرر الإكاف، وينبغي حمله على ما إذا أسرجه بسرج يسرج بمثله الحمر، أما إذا كان لا يسرج بمثله الحمر فإنه يضمن كما هنا فلا مخالفة بينهما فتأمل قوله: (وكذا إذا أبدله لأن الحمار الخ) أي وكذا لا يضمن. وعبارة غاية البيان وقال الكرخي في مختصره: إن لم يكن عليه لجام فألجمه فلا ضمان عليه إذا كان مثله يلجم بذلك اللجام، وكذلك إن أبدله وذلك لأن الحمار لا يختلف باللجام وغيره ولا يتلف به فلم يضمن بالجامه والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وهو الموفق والمعين قال أستاذنا مؤلف هذه الحواشي
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is contrary in it. The saddle and the pack-saddle, or saddling with something not similar, and taking a path other than specified and difference... He said: (And removing the saddle and pack-saddle and saddling with something not similar to it) means if one hires a donkey with a saddle then removes the saddle and saddles it with a saddle not similar to what is usually saddled on donkeys, or puts a packsaddle on it absolutely, or removes the packsaddle and saddles with something not similar, and it perishes, he is liable for its full value...
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by commentary. The author discusses the scenario where a hirer of a donkey changes the equipment (saddle or packsaddle) to something not similar or of a different kind. The key principle: if the new equipment is of a different genus (jins) and not customarily used for the animal, the hirer becomes liable for full compensation if the animal dies, because he causes a change that is detrimental. The analogy is made to someone who replaces wheat with iron in a contract. If the equipment is similar (like replacing one saddle with another of the same type), there is no liability. There is a partial difference from Shuyukh regarding the place of riding; in long-distance travel, the custom may exempt liability. The relied-upon position (al-madhhab) from al-Kafi is absolute liability because it is the clear transmission (zahir al-riwayah). Later, it is mentioned that if the animal is ridden without any equipment, liability depends on the status of the hirer (noble or commoner). The passage also covers the case of putting a bridle (lujam) — since donkeys are not affected by bridles, there is no liability unless the bridle is of a type not used for such donkeys.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Custom; common practice that can influence legal rulings.
الأشراف (al-ashraf): Noblemen; people of status who customarily ride with proper equipment.
العوام (al-awamm): Commoners; ordinary people who may ride bare.
اللجام (al-lujam): Bridle; headgear for a donkey or horse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shuyukh's distinction, if a nobleman hires a donkey in the city and changes the saddle to a packsaddle, and the donkey perishes, what is the liability?
A) Full liability because the change of genus applies.
B) No liability because he is noble and riding in the city.
C) Liability only for the difference in value.
D) Half liability.

Key Takeaway
Custom and status can create exceptions to the general rule of liability, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is absolute liability regardless of these factors.

Liability for Deviating from the Specified Route in Ijarah
Explains the ruling when the hirer or carrier deviates from the specified route causing loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for liability when a hired animal is taken on a different route, and apply the ruling to cases involving tafawut.

Core Idea
Liability for route deviation hinges on tafawut — if the alternative route is equally safe, no liability.

In ijarah contracts, the carrier must follow the agreed route. If they deviate, liability for loss depends on whether the deviation introduced additional risk. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, focusing on the crucial condition of tafawut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
The act is taking a hired animal on a route different from the one specified. Default: if no route was specified, deviation does not trigger liability.
Only if the route was explicitly stated does deviation become relevant.
2
Recognize the condition of specification
Liability only arises when the route was actually specified in the contract. Without specification, the hirer has no restricted duty.
The text says: 'قيد بالتعيين لأنه لو لم يعين لا ضمان.'
3
Determine the importance of tafawut
Even if the route was specified, liability requires that the alternative route has tafawut – a meaningful difference in distance, safety, or difficulty that makes the specification beneficial.
If both routes are equal, no liability: 'إذا تساويا لا ضمان.'
4
Apply the ruling to the given examples
The text provides two examples: a porter who unnecessarily lingers in a desert is liable; a carrier who takes a sea route when land was stipulated is liable due to increased risk.
These illustrate that tafawut can be geographic (longer/rougher) or contextual (dangerous delay).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية البيان قوله: (وسلوك طريق غير ما عينه وتفاوتاً) أي يجب الضمان إذا عين للمكاري طريقاً أو لمستأجر الدابة طريقاً وسلك غيره وكان بينهما تفاوت بأن كان المسلوك أبعد أو أوعر أو أخوف بحيث لا يسلك لصحة التقييد بكونه مفيداً، وأما إذا كان بحيث يسلك فظاهر الكتاب أنه إن كان بينهما تفاوت ضمن وإلا فلا. وأشار إلى أنهما لو تساويا لا ضمان، وقيد بالتعيين لأنه لو لم يعين لا ضمان. وفي الخلاصة: الحمال إذا نزل في مفازة وتهيأ له الانتقال فلم ينتقل حتى فسدت المتاع بمطر أو سرقة فهو ضامن إذا كانت السرقة والمطر غالباً قوله: وحمله في البحر الكل أي يضمن بحمله في البحر إذا قيد بالبر لأن التقييد مفيد بخطر البحر وبندرة السلامة فيه. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مما يسلكه الناس أو لا، وقيدنا بكونه قيد بالبر لأنه لو لم يقيد به لا ضمان
The commentary of Ghayah al-Bayan: (And taking a path other than specified and difference) i.e., liability is necessary if a path is specified for the carrier or the hirer of the animal and he takes a different path and there is a difference such that the taken path is farther, rougher, or more dangerous so that the specification is valid. If the path is such that it is traversed anyway, then according to the apparent text, if there is a difference, he is liable; otherwise no. He indicated that if they are equal, no liability, and the condition is specification; if not specified, no liability. And in al-Khulasa: If the porter alights in a desert and is able to move on but does not until the goods spoil due to rain or theft, he is liable if rain and theft are common. He said: And carrying it in the sea, i.e., he is liable if he carries it by sea when stipulated land travel, because the stipulation is beneficial due to the danger of the sea and rarity of safety.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for deviating from the stipulated route in an ijarah contract. The key condition for liability is: (1) the route was specified, (2) the actual route differs in being longer, rougher, or more dangerous, and (3) the difference is such that the specification was meaningful (tafwit). If the alternative route is equally good, no liability. An example from al-Khulasa illustrates when a porter unnecessarily delays in a dangerous place, leading to loss. Additionally, if the contract specified land travel but the carrier goes by sea, he is liable due to the increased risk. The ruling distinguishes between cases where the specification is beneficial and when it is not.

Key Terms
سلوك طريق غير ما عينه (suluk tariq ghayr ma 'ayyanah): Taking a path other than the one specified in the contract for the journey.
التفاوت (al-tafawut): The difference between the specified route and the actual route in terms of distance, safety, or difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hirer specifies land travel for a hired camel, but the carrier takes a sea route. The camel perishes. According to the passage, what is the ruling?
A) No liability because the camel would have perished on land too.
B) The carrier is liable because the sea route is more dangerous and the stipulation was beneficial.
C) Only half compensation because sea travel is not inherently forbidden.
D) Liability only if the camel owner objects.

Key Takeaway
Liability for route deviation in ijarah requires specification and tafawut; without a meaningful difference, no compensation is due.

Wage Entitlement Upon Delivery of Goods
Comments on the wage trigger for a porter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a porter's wage to become due and explain why wage and prior liability are not mutually exclusive.

Core Idea
Wage is due upon delivery; liability for loss en route does not cancel the wage for completed service.

In Hanafi fiqh, the wage of a porter (or any hired carrier) is not earned simply by undertaking the journey. The crucial moment is delivery. This short commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the wording 'balagha' can be read in two ways but the ruling is the same. Moreover, it resolves a potential confusion: if the porter was liable for damage before delivery, can he still claim his wage? The answer is yes, because the two obligations arise in different states.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly: the wage becomes obligatory (wajib) when the goods reach the stipulated location. This is the key legal conclusion.
The text says 'wajaba al-ajr' (wage becomes obligatory).
2
Examine the linguistic note
The word 'balagha' can be read with tashdid (porter causes arrival) or takhfif (goods themselves arrive). Both readings lead to the same ruling, so the legal effect is unaffected.
This shows that linguistic variants do not affect the fiqh ruling if the meaning is consistent.
3
Understand the rationale
The wage becomes due because the 'dispute is removed' — the risk of loss or damage en route is over. Delivery marks completion of the service.
Before delivery, there is uncertainty; after delivery, the porter's obligation is fulfilled.
4
Resolve the apparent conflict
The text states that wage and liability are not combined because they occur in different states: liability arises if loss occurs before delivery, while wage is earned after delivery. They do not coexist simultaneously.
Thus, a porter who was liable for damage en route still receives his wage once he delivers the goods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن بلغ فله الأجر قال الأتقاني: السماع بالتشديد أي وإن بلغ الحمال المتاع ذلك الموضع الذي اشترطه ويجوز بالتخفيف على إسناد الفعل إلى المتاع أي إذا بلغ المتاع إلى ذلك الموضع وإنما وجب الأجر لارتفاع الخلاف ولا يلزم اجتماع الأجر والضمان لأنهما في حالتين
He said: (And if it arrives, then he has the wage) Al-Atqani said: 'al-sama' with tashdid, meaning if the porter delivers the goods to the place he stipulated, and it is permissible with takhif by attributing the action to the goods, i.e., when the goods reach that place. And the wage becomes obligatory because the dispute is removed, and it is not necessary to combine wage and liability because they are in two different states.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a brief comment on the matn: 'Wa in balagha falahu al-ajr.' It clarifies that the porter's wage is due upon delivery to the specified place. The word 'balagha' can be read with tashdid (emphasized) meaning the porter causes it to reach, or with takhfif (light) meaning the goods themselves reach. In either case, the wage is obligatory because the risk of loss from the journey is over. Importantly, the wage and liability for compensation do not co-exist in the same state; if the goods are lost en route, the porter may be liable, but once delivered, he is entitled to the wage and no further liability.

Key Terms
الأجر (al-ajr): The wage due to the porter for completing the transportation service.
الوصول (al-wusul): The arrival of the goods at the agreed location.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability for compensation due to loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A porter agrees to carry goods from city A to city B. On the way, the goods are damaged due to his negligence (he is liable). He then repairs them and delivers them to B. Is he entitled to the wage?
A) Yes, because delivery occurred.
B) No, because he was liable for damage.
C) Only half the wage.
D) Only if he was not liable for the damage.

Key Takeaway
A porter's wage is due upon delivery to the agreed place, and prior liability for damage does not preclude the wage, as they relate to different states.

Liability for Planting a More Harmful Crop on Leased Land
Ruling when a tenant plants a more damaging crop than permitted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a tenant plants a more or less harmful crop than permitted and apply the qiyas to the ghasib principle.

Core Idea
A tenant who plants a more harmful crop than permitted is a usurper—liable for damage and forfeits the wage.

In Ijara (lease) contracts, the use of the land is specified. If the tenant deviates and causes greater harm, the contract is breached. The Hanafi school uses qiyas (analogy) to ghasp (usurpation) to determine liability. This lesson examines the ruling from Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the tenant did (planted a different crop) and whether the crop is more or less harmful than permitted. The ruling depends on this condition.
The text says: 'إذا زرع رطبة وقد أذن له بزرع الحنطة' – the tenant planted alfalfa when permitted wheat.
2
Apply the condition of harm
Check if the planted crop is more harmful. The commentary states alfalfa is more harmful. If it were less harmful, the ruling would be the opposite.
The condition is explicit: 'قيد بكون ما زرعه أشد ضرراً' – it is conditioned that what he planted is more harmful.
3
Identify the legal analogy (qiyas)
The tenant is analogized to a ghasib (misappropriator) because both exceed the scope of permission and cause harm. The shared effective cause (illa) is exceeding permission and causing damage.
The text says: 'لأنه غاصب' – because he is a usurper.
4
Derive the consequences
Like a ghasib, the tenant must compensate for the decrease in land value and is not entitled to any wage.
The text: 'ضمن ما نقص من الأرض' and 'ولا يجب الأجر المسمى ولا غيره'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبزرع رطبة وأذن بالبر ما نقص ولا أجر) أي ضمن ما نقص من الأرض إذا زرع رطبة وقد أذن له بزرع الحنطة لأن الرطاب أكثر ضرراً بالأرض من الحنطة، ولا يجب الأجر المسمى ولا غيره لأنه غاصب قيد بكون ما زرعه أشد ضرراً لأنه لو كان أنقص ضرراً لا ضمان ويجب الأجر
He said: (And if he plants alfalfa and gave permission for wheat, then what is diminished [in value] and no wage) i.e., he is liable for the deficiency in the land if he plants alfalfa while the permission was for wheat, because alfalfa is more harmful to the land than wheat, and he is not owed the named wage nor anything else because he is a usurper. It is conditioned that what he planted is more harmful; if it were less harmful, there would be no liability and the wage would be owed.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn discussing a contract where land is leased for planting a specific crop. If the tenant plants a different crop that is more harmful to the land (e.g., alfalfa instead of wheat), he is considered a usurper (ghasib) and must compensate for the decrease in land value. He is not entitled to any wage (the agreed-upon rent or otherwise). However, if the crop he plants is less harmful, he is not liable for damage and even entitled to the wage. The reasoning is that the permission was for a less harmful use, and exceeding it with a more harmful use violates the contract.

Key Terms
الرطبة (al-ratbah): Alfalfa or a type of fodder crop that is known to deplete soil nutrients more than wheat.
الحنطة (al-hintah): Wheat, a less harmful crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A farmer leases land to grow wheat but instead plants a milder crop (less harmful). What is the ruling?
A) He must compensate for the difference and gets no wage.
B) He is not liable for damage and is entitled to the wage.
C) He is liable only if the land value decreases.
D) He forfeits the wage but owes nothing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling differentiates between more and less harmful crop changes: causing increased harm triggers liability and loss of wage, while less harm does not.

Carrier Deviation and Sea Route Liability
Explaining liability for carrier deviation and sea carriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a carrier becomes liable for deviating from a specified route or for using a sea route when land was stipulated, and apply the ruling to new hire contracts.

Core Idea
Deviation from a beneficial condition triggers liability; the wage is earned only upon safe delivery.

This passage from Ghāyat al-Bayān explains the liability of a carrier (mukārī) or animal lessee when they deviate from the route specified in the hire contract or carry goods by sea when land was stipulated. The key is whether the condition was beneficial to the contract: if the deviation involves a harmful difference or if sea carriage is inherently dangerous, the carrier is liable. The wage is earned only if the goods arrive safely, and liability and wage do not coexist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is transporting goods under a hire contract (ijārah). The ruling concerns whether the carrier is liable (ḍamān) for loss if he deviates from the specified route or uses an unauthorized mode (sea instead of land).
2
Locate the condition for liability
Liability arises only if the route was specified (ta'yīn) and the deviation involves a harmful difference (tafāwut): the taken path is farther, rougher, or more dangerous such that people would not normally travel it. If the deviation is not harmful and the roads are comparable, according to Ẓāhir al-Kitāb, liability still applies if there is any difference; if equal, no liability.
If no route was specified, deviation does not trigger liability.
3
Apply the rule to sea carriage
If the contract restricts carriage to land but the carrier uses sea, he is liable because the sea is dangerous and safety is rare. The restriction is beneficial, so breaching it triggers liability.
This applies even if the sea route is commonly used by others.
4
Separate liability from wage entitlement
The carrier gets the wage (ajr) only if the goods are delivered to the stipulated place. Liability for loss occurs if the goods are damaged or lost due to the deviation or sea carriage. These two are in separate states: liability is incurred when loss occurs; wage is earned upon safe delivery.
They do not combine because the wage is for successful performance.
5
Identify the basis of the ruling
The ruling is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference) and custom (ʿurf). The condition specifying route or mode is beneficial; breaching it invalidates the benefit, so the carrier becomes liable. This is a principle of fair dealing in hire contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية البيان قوله: (وسلوك طريق غير ما عينه وتفاوتاً) أي يجب الضمان إذا عين للمكاري طريقاً أو لمستأجر الدابة طريقاً وسلك غيره وكان بينهما تفاوت بأن كان المسلوك أبعد أو أوعر أو أخوف بحيث لا يسلك لصحة التقييد بكونه مفيداً، وأما إذا كان بحيث يسلك فظاهر الكتاب أنه إن كان بينهما تفاوت ضمن وإلا فلا. وأشار إلى أنهما لو تساويا لا ضمان، وقيد بالتعيين لأنه لو لم يعين لا ضمان. وفي الخلاصة : الحمال إذا نزل في مفازة وتهيأ له الانتقال فلم ينتقل حتى فسدت المتاع بمطر أو سرقة فهو ضامن إذا كانت السرقة والمطر غالباً قوله : وحمله في البحر الكل أي يضمن بحمله في البحر إذا قيد بالبر لأن التقييد مفيد بخطر البحر وبندرة السلامة فيه. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مما يسلكه الناس أو لا، وقيدنا بكونه قيد بالبر لأنه لو لم يقيد به لا ضمان قوله : (وإن بلغ فله الأجر قال الأتقاني : السماع بالتشديد أي وإن بلغ الحمال المتاع ذلك الموضع الذي اشترطه ويجوز بالتخفيف على إسناد الفعل إلى المتاع أي إذا بلغ المتاع إلى ذلك الموضع وإنما وجب الأجر لارتفاع الخلاف ولا يلزم اجتماع الأجر والضمان لأنهما في حالتين
Ghāyat al-Bayān: His saying: (And taking a path other than what he specified and a difference) meaning: liability is obligatory if he specified a path for the carrier or for the lessee of the animal and he took another path and there was a difference between them, such that the taken path was farther, rougher, or more dangerous, such that one would not travel it due to the validity of the restriction being beneficial. But if it was such that one would travel it, then Ẓāhir al-Kitāb states: if there is a difference between them, he is liable; otherwise not. And he indicated that if they are equal, there is no liability. And he restricted it with specification, because if he did not specify, there is no liability. And in al-Khulāṣah: The porter, if he descends in a desert and is able to move but does not move until the goods are spoiled by rain or theft, he is liable if the theft and rain are predominant. His saying: And his carrying in the sea: everything, meaning he is liable for carrying it in the sea if he restricted to land, because the restriction is beneficial due to the danger of the sea and the rarity of safety therein. He made it absolute, so it includes whether it is something that people travel or not, and we restricted it to his having restricted to land, because if he did not restrict, there is no liability. His saying: (And if it arrives, he gets the wage). al-Atqānī said: al-samāʿ with tashdīd, meaning if the porter delivers the goods to that place which he stipulated, and it is permissible with takhfīf based on attributing the action to the goods, i.e., if the goods reach that place. The wage is only obligatory because the disagreement is removed, and it does not necessitate the combination of wage and liability because they are in two states.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ghāyat al-Bayān explaining rulings on carrier liability. It first addresses when a carrier deviates from a specified route: if the deviation involves a harmful difference (farther, rougher, or more dangerous), the carrier is liable for damages. If no harmful difference, no liability. The key condition is that the route must have been specified; if unspecified, no liability for deviation. Then it discusses carrying goods in the sea when the contract specified land: the carrier is liable for any loss because the sea route is dangerous. If the goods arrive safely, he gets his wage. The commentator clarifies that liability and wage do not coexist in the same situation: liability occurs if goods are lost, wage is earned if delivered. The ruling is based on custom (ʿurf) and istiḥsān (juristic preference).

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage; here, the carrier must pay for goods lost due to deviation or sea carriage.
أجر (ajr): Wage or payment for service; here, the carrier's fee is earned upon delivery.
تفاوت (tafāwut): Difference or disparity; here, the harmful difference between the specified and taken route that triggers liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a carrier liable for deviating from a specified route?
A) Whenever he deviates, regardless of the difference.
B) Only if the new route is farther, rougher, or more dangerous and the deviation is harmful.
C) Only if the deviation causes the goods to be lost.
D) He is never liable if the route was not specified.

Key Takeaway
A carrier is liable for loss or damage when he deviates from a beneficial condition in the contract, especially if the deviation involves a harmful difference or unauthorized mode like sea instead of land.

Planting a Different Crop on Leased Land: Liability and Wage
Ruling on liability and wage when a planter grows a different crop than permitted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a lessee plants a crop more harmful than permitted, and explain the basis for liability and denial of wage.

Core Idea
Planting a crop more harmful than authorized makes the planter a usurper (ghāṣib) liable for damage and forfeits his wage.

In agricultural leases, the lessee must follow the agreed crop. If he plants a different crop that causes more harm to the land, does he still deserve the wage? The author of al-Bahr al-Rāʼiq explains that the degree of harm determines both liability and entitlement to the wage. Let's examine the legal reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What did the lessee do? (Planted reeds instead of wheat). State the two consequences: liability for decrease in land value, and forfeiture of the wage.
2
Locate the dalil
The author states the ruling because the planter becomes a ghāṣib (usurper). Identify the proof: the general rule that a ghāṣib is liable for damage and not entitled to compensation.
The proof is not a direct textual source but a legal principle (qiyas on ghaṣb).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does being a ghāṣib lead to this ruling? Exceeding authorization ('udwan) causes damage, so liability follows. No wage because the ghāṣib's work is not based on a valid contract.
4
Note the condition
The text restricts the ruling to when the planted crop is more harmful. Understand the counter-case: if less harmful, no liability and wage is due.
This is a taqyid (restriction) based on the concept of ḍarar.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
What is the practical effect? The lessor is compensated for damage, and the lessee loses his wage, discouraging harmful deviations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبزرع رطبة وأذن بالبر ما نقص ولا أجر) أي ضمن ما نقص من الأرض إذا زرع رطبة وقد أذن له بزرع الحنطة لأن الرطاب أكثر ضرراً بالأرض من الحنطة، ولا يجب الأجر المسمى ولا غيره لأنه غاصب قيد بكون ما زرعه أشد ضرراً لأنه لو كان أنقص ضرراً لا ضمان ويجب الأجر
His saying: (And he planted reeds and he authorized wheat: what is decreased [is liable] and no wage) meaning: he is liable for what decreased from the land if he planted reeds while he had been authorized to plant wheat, because reeds are more harmful to the land than wheat. And the named wage is not obligatory nor any other, because he is a usurper (ghāṣib). It is restricted to his having planted something more harmful; because if it were less harmful, there would be no liability and wage would be obligatory.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling concerning a lease of land for agriculture. The lessee is permitted to plant wheat (ḥinṭa) but instead plants reeds (raṭba), which are more harmful to the soil. The ruling: the lessee is liable (ḍāmin) for the decrease in the land's value caused by the harmful crop. Additionally, he does not receive the agreed wage (or any wage) because by exceeding the authorization, he becomes a ghāṣib (usurper) and thus not entitled to payment. However, if the unauthorized crop is less harmful (e.g., planting something less damaging than wheat), then there is no liability and the wage is due. The key condition is the degree of harm: more harm leads to liability and no wage; less harm leads to no liability and wage.

Key Terms
غاصب (ghāṣib): One who unlawfully takes or uses another's property without permission; here, the planter becomes a usurper by exceeding authorization.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm or damage; the degree of harm determines liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a planter is authorized to plant wheat but plants barley, which is less harmful to the land?
A) He is liable for the decrease and receives no wage.
B) He is not liable and receives the wage.
C) He is liable but receives the wage.
D) He is not liable and receives no wage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi Ijara, the degree of harm from an unauthorized crop determines both liability for damage and entitlement to the wage.

Owner's Options When a Tailor Deviates from Instructions
Hanafi ruling with proof on tailor's deviation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the owner's two options when a tailor sews a different garment than ordered, and explain why the fair wage (ajr al-mithl) applies instead of the named wage.

Core Idea
Deviating tailor: owner may accept altered garment with fair wage or demand cloth's value.

When you give a tailor a cloth and specify a garment, but he sews something else, what are your rights? The Hanafi school gives you a choice: accept the altered garment and pay a fair wage, or reject it and claim the cloth's value. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the option applies when the tailor cuts and reshapes the cloth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deviation
The tailor was ordered to sew a qamīṣ (long shirt) but sewed a qabā (outer coat). The key is that the qabā resembles a qamīṣ in usage among Turks, so it is a partial compliance.
If the garment were completely different (e.g., trousers), the same ruling applies in the soundest view.
2
Determine the owner's options
The owner may either accept the qabā and pay the fair wage (ajr al-mithl), or reject it and hold the tailor liable for the value of the cloth.
These are the two options: acceptance with fair wage or rejection with full compensation.
3
Explain why ajr al-mithl is paid, not the named wage
The named wage was agreed only on the condition that the purpose (sewing a qamīṣ) be fully achieved. Since the purpose was not met, the contractual wage falls away, and the fair market wage for the actual benefit (the qabā) is owed instead.
This is based on the principle that the named wage is contingent on full achievement of the intended benefit.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Asbījābī held that if the tailor cuts and changes the shape (the second scenario), the owner has no option; only liability for the cloth value applies. The commentator rejects this, supporting the option as the sounder (al-aṣaḥḥ) view.
The majority Hanafi position preserves the option even when the cloth is physically altered.
5
Apply to analogous cases from al-Khulāṣah
Similar rulings apply to dyers who dye the wrong color and tailors who cut deficient lengths or mislead about cloth sufficiency. In each, the owner's option depends on whether the deviation is significant (excessive) and whether the craftsman acted intentionally or negligently.
These cases reinforce the general principle that deviation from instructions triggers the owner's choice and fair compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبخياطة قباء وأمر بقميص قيمة ثوبه وله أخذ القباء ودفع أجر مثله لأنه لما كان يشبه القميص من وجه لأن الأتراك يستعملونه استعمال القميص كان موافقاً من وجه من وجه، فإن شاء مال إلى جانب الوفاق وأخذ الثوب وإن شاء مال إلى جانب الخلاف وضمنه القيمة. وإنما وجب أجر المثل دون المسمى لأن صاحبه إنما رضي بالمسمى عند حصول المقصود من كل وجه ولم يحصل . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان يستعمل استعمال القميص وما إذا شقه وجعله قباء خلافاً للأسبيجابي في الثاني حيث أوجب فيه الضمان من غير خيار، وسيأتي أنهما لو اختلفا في المأمور به فالقول لرب الثوب، والتقييد بالقباء اتفاقي إذ لو خاطه سراويل وقد أمره بالقباء كان الحكم كذلك على الأصح. وفي الخلاصة : والصباغ إذا خالف فصبغ الأصفر مكان الأحمر إن شاء ضمنه قيمة ثوب أبيض، وإن شاء أخذه وأعطاه ما زاد الصبغ فيه ولا أجر له، ولو صبغ رديئاً إن لم يكن فاحشاً لا يضمن. وإن كان فاحشاً بحيث يقول أهل تلك الصنعة إنه فاحش يضمن قيمة ثوب أبيض. وفيها أيضاً: رجل دفع إلى خياط ثوباً وقال له اقطعه حتى يصيب القدم وكمه خمسة أشبار وعرضه كذا فجاء به ناقصاً إن كان قدر أصبع ونحوه فليس بشيء، وإن كان أكثر يضمنه. وفيها أيضاً: ولو قال للخياط انظر إلى هذا الثوب إن كفاني قميصاً فاقطعه بدرهم وخيطه ثم قال إنه لا يكفيك يضمن الثوب، ولو قال انظر أيكفيني قميصاً فقال نعم فقال اقطعه ثم قال لا يكفيك لا يضمن والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
His saying: (And with sewing a qabā while he ordered a qamīṣ: the value of his cloth, and he has the option to take the qabā and pay its fair wage.) Because it resembles a qamīṣ in some respects, since the Turks use it like a qamīṣ, so it is in agreement in some aspects. Thus if he wishes, he may incline towards agreement and take the garment; if he wishes, he may incline towards disagreement and hold him liable for the value. And only the fair wage (ajr al-mithl) is obligatory, not the named wage, because the owner only consented to the named wage when the purpose was fully achieved, and it was not achieved. He made it absolute, so it includes whether it is used like a qamīṣ or whether he tore it and made it a qabā, contrary to al-Asbījābī in the second case, who made liability without option. And it will come that if they differ about what was ordered, the word is with the owner of the cloth. The restriction to qabā is incidental; if he sewed trousers when ordered to sew a qabā, the ruling is the same in the soundest view. And in al-Khulāṣah: The dyer if he violates and dyes yellow instead of red: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for the value of a white cloth; if he wishes, he may take it and pay him the increase from the dye, and there is no wage for him. And if he dyes poorly, if it is not excessive, he is not liable; if it is excessive such that the people of that trade say it is excessive, he is liable for the value of a white cloth. And also in it: A man gave a cloth to a tailor and said: cut it so that it reaches the foot, and its sleeve is five spans and its width is such, and he brought it deficient: if it is about a finger or similar, it is nothing; if more, he is liable for it. And also in it: If he said to the tailor: look at this cloth, if it suffices for a qamīṣ, cut it for a dirham and sew it, then he said it does not suffice, he is liable for the cloth. And if he said: look, does it suffice for a qamīṣ? He said yes, then he said cut it, then he said it does not suffice, he is not liable. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling about a tailor who sews a different garment (qabā) than ordered (qamīṣ). Since a qabā resembles a qamīṣ in usage (like the Turks wear it similarly), the owner has two options: (1) agree and take the qabā, paying the fair wage (ajr al-mithl), or (2) disagree and hold the tailor liable for the value of the cloth. The owner's wage is only the fair wage, not the agreed amount, because the purpose was not fully achieved. The commentator notes that some scholars (al-Asbījābī) differ when the tailor actually cuts and changes the cloth, saying there is no option and only liability. The passage also includes rulings from al-Khulāṣah about dyers violating color orders (yellow instead of red) and similar cases, as well as cases of tailoring with deficient dimensions or misleading statements. In all cases, the principle is that the craftsman is liable if he deviates from instructions in a harmful way.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Fair market wage for the service, not the agreed wage, because the purpose was not fully achieved.
خيار (khiyār): Option or choice given to the owner to either take the altered garment or demand compensation.
قيمة الثوب (qīmat al-thawb): The market value of the cloth, which the tailor must pay if the owner rejects the altered garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the owner pay ajr al-mithl instead of the named wage when accepting the altered garment?
A) Because the tailor refused to accept the named wage.
B) Because the owner's consent to the named wage was conditional on full achievement of the purpose.
C) Because ajr al-mithl is always lower than the named wage.
D) Because the tailor deviated intentionally.

Key Takeaway
When a craftsman deviates from instructions, the recipient may either accept the work with a fair wage or demand compensation for the material's value.

Distinguishing Fāsid from Bāṭil in Hire Contracts
Defining fāsid ijārah and distinguishing from bāṭil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a fāsid (invalid) and bāṭil (void) hire contract in Hanafi law, and state the legal consequence for each regarding wage obligation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a fāsid ijārah requires payment of fair wage (ajr al-mithl) for usage, while a bāṭil ijārah gives no wage at all.

This passage opens the chapter on fāsid ijārah with a clear definition and distinction. It explains that a bāṭil contract is unlawful in essence, so usage creates no wage obligation. In contrast, a fāsid contract is lawful in essence but defective in description; once used, it obligates the hirer to pay the fair market wage (ajr al-mithl). The commentator also contrasts this with sale, where a fāsid sale transfers ownership upon possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two concepts defined
The passage defines fāsid and bāṭil contracts. Recognize that both are types of defective contracts, but they differ in fundamentality.
Fāsid is lawful in essence (aṣl) but defective in description (waṣf). Bāṭil is unlawful in essence entirely.
2
Note the criterion for distinction
The key criterion is whether the contract is lawful in its essence (mashrūʿ bi-aṣlihī). Bāṭil lacks this entirely; fāsid has it.
This is a Hanafi-specific taxonomy; other schools may not distinguish as sharply.
3
Derive the ruling for each
For bāṭil: no wage is due for usage (lā yajibu bihi bi-l-istiʿmāl ajr). For fāsid: if usage occurred, ajr al-mithl is wajib.
Ajr al-mithl is the fair market wage, not the named rent.
4
Recognize the contrast with sale
The passage notes that in a fāsid sale, ownership transfers by possession (qabḍ), but in a fāsid hire, usage does not transfer ownership; it only obligates ajr al-mithl.
This distinction affects how the two contracts are rectified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإجارة الفاسدة وهي كل عقد كان مشروعاً بأصله دون وصفه. وبين الفاسد والباطل هنا فرق أيضاً فإن الباطل ما ليس بمشروع أصلاً وحكمه أنه لا يجب فيه بالاستعمال أجر بخلاف الفاسد فإنه يجب فيه به أجرة المثل؛ صرح به في الحقائق شرح المنظومة في مسألة إجارة المشاع، وهكذا في جامع الفضولين لكن بين الإجارة والبيع فرق فإن الفاسد من البيع يملك بالقبض
Chapter on Invalid Hire (al-Ijārah al-Fāsida). And it is every contract that is lawful in its essence but not in its description. And between the invalid (fāsid) and void (bāṭil) here there is also a difference: for the void is what is not lawful in essence at all, and its ruling is that usage does not necessitate a wage, contrary to the invalid, for which istihqāq of ajr al-mithl is obligatory for usage; this is stated in al-Ḥaqāʾiq Sharḥ al-Manẓūma in the issue of leasing undivided property (ijārat al-mushāʿ), and likewise in Jāmiʿ al-Fuḍūlayn. But there is a difference between hire and sale: the invalid (fāsid) in sale becomes owned by possession (qabḍ).
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a new chapter defining an invalid (fāsid) hire contract. It distinguishes fāsid from bāṭil: a bāṭil contract is unlawful in its very essence (e.g., leasing a thing that cannot be leased at all), so no wage is due for usage. A fāsid contract is lawful in essence (e.g., the subject matter is valid) but defective in description (e.g., a condition invalidates it). Such a contract, if actually used, requires payment of the fair wage (ajr al-mithl). The commentator notes that this distinction is consistent with other works and highlights a difference between hire and sale: in sale, a fāsid contract transfers ownership of the object upon possession (qabḍ), whereas in hire, usage does not transfer ownership but still requires fair compensation.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsida): A hire contract lawful in essence but defective in a description, e.g., an invalid condition.
أجرة المثل (ajrat al-mithl): Fair market wage for the usage, not the named wage, due to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a contract is void (bāṭil) in ijarah?
A) Usage requires ajr al-mithl.
B) Usage requires the named wage.
C) Usage does not require any wage.
D) It is the same as fāsid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes fāsid (invalid) from bāṭil (void) in hire: usage of a fāsid contract obligates ajr al-mithl, while a bāṭil contract gives no right to any wage.
