Corrupt Lease: Tailor's Deviation and Ujrat al-Mithl
Ruling on corrupt lease conditions with example of tailor and dyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a condition corrupting the lease obliges ujrat al-mithl not exceeding the named wage and identify the owner's options when the worker deviates.

Core Idea
A tailor's deviation by making a qaba instead of a qamis corrupts the lease; the owner may accept the work with ujrat al-mithl or reject it and claim the cloth's value.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi ruling on corrupt leases when the hired worker deviates from instructions. The passage establishes that any condition contrary to the contract's nature corrupts the lease, but the contract is not void; rather, the worker is entitled to the market rate capped by the named wage. The owner has options depending on the degree of deviation, reflecting the underlying reasoning of partial conformity or total non-conformity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the general rule: a condition corrupting the lease makes it fasid, and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl not exceeding the named wage.
The named wage (musamma) is the cap.
2
Analyse the tailor example
Examine the example: tailor ordered to sew a qamis but sews a qaba. Owner has two options: accept the qaba and pay ujrat al-mithl, or reject and claim cloth value.
Partial resemblance (qaba used like qamis by Turks) gives option.
3
Understand the illah
The reasoning (illah) is that the owner consented to the named wage only for full conformity; partial conformity justifies ujrat al-mithl.
Total non-conformity would eliminate the option to take.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Asbajabi holds that splitting the cloth to make a qaba gives no option; the majority grants the option. Mufta bihi is the majority.
The text favors the option view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإجارة الفاسدة
يفسد الإجارة الشرط وله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى.
قوله : (وبخياطة قباء وأمر بقميص قيمة ثوبه وله أخذ القباء ودفع أجر مثله لأنه لما كان يشبه القميص من وجه لأن الأتراك يستعملونه استعمال القميص كان موافقاً من وجه من وجه، فإن شاء مال إلى جانب الوفاق وأخذ الثوب وإن شاء مال إلى جانب الخلاف وضمنه القيمة. وإنما وجب أجر المثل دون المسمى لأن صاحبه إنما رضي بالمسمى عند حصول المقصود من كل وجه ولم يحصل . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان يستعمل استعمال القميص وما إذا شقه وجعله قباء خلافاً للأسبيجابي في الثاني حيث أوجب فيه الضمان من غير خيار، وسيأتي أنهما لو اختلفا في المأمور به فالقول لرب الثوب، والتقييد بالقباء اتفاقي إذ لو خاطه سراويل وقد أمره بالقباء كان الحكم كذلك على الأصح. وفي الخلاصة : والصباغ إذا خالف فصبغ الأصفر مكان الأحمر إن شاء ضمنه قيمة ثوب أبيض، وإن شاء أخذه وأعطاه ما زاد الصبغ فيه ولا أجر له، ولو صبغ رديئاً إن لم يكن فاحشاً لا يضمن. وإن كان فاحشاً بحيث يقول أهل تلك الصنعة إنه فاحش يضمن قيمة ثوب أبيض. وفيها أيضاً: رجل دفع إلى خياط ثوباً وقال له اقطعه حتى يصيب القدم وكمه خمسة أشبار وعرضه كذا فجاء به ناقصاً إن كان قدر أصبع ونحوه فليس بشيء، وإن كان أكثر يضمنه. وفيها أيضاً: ولو قال للخياط انظر إلى هذا الثوب إن كفاني قميصاً فاقطعه بدرهم وخيطه ثم قال إنه لا يكفيك يضمن الثوب، ولو قال انظر أيكفيني قميصاً فقال نعم فقال اقطعه ثم قال لا يكفيك لا يضمن والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Chapter of Fasid Lease: The condition corrupts the lease, and he has its equivalent wage, not exceeding the named [wage]. His statement: (And regarding sewing a qaba while he ordered a qamis: the value of his cloth, and he may take the qaba and pay its equivalent wage, because since it resembles the qamis in one respect because the Turks use it as a qamis, it is conforming in one respect and opposing in another. If he wishes, he may incline to the side of conformity and take the cloth, and if he wishes, he may incline to the side of opposition and guarantee its value. And the equivalent wage is obligatory, not the named wage, because its owner only consented to the named wage upon the occurrence of the intended purpose from every respect, and it did not occur. He made it absolute, so it includes when it is used as a qamis and when he splits it and makes it a qaba, contrary to al-Asbajabi in the second, where he imposed guarantee without option. And it will come that if they differ about what was ordered, the word is of the cloth owner, and the restriction to qaba is incidental, for if he sewed it into sirwal while he ordered a qaba, the ruling is likewise according to the most correct. And in al-Khulasa: And the dyer, if he deviates and dyes yellow instead of red, if he wishes, he guarantees the value of a white cloth, and if he wishes, he takes it and gives him what the dye increased, and he has no wage. And if he dyes defectively, if it is not excessive, he does not guarantee; if it is excessive such that the people of that craft say it is excessive, he guarantees the value of a white cloth. And in it also: A man gave a tailor a cloth and said to him, 'Cut it to fit the foot, with its sleeve five spans and its width such-and-such,' and he brought it deficient: if it was about a finger's length or similar, it is nothing; if it was more, he guarantees it. And in it also: If he said to the tailor, 'Look at this cloth; if it suffices me for a qamis, then cut it for a dirham and sew it,' then he said, 'It does not suffice you,' he guarantees the cloth. And if he said, 'Look, does it suffice me for a qamis?' and he said, 'Yes,' then he said, 'Cut it,' then he said, 'It does not suffice,' he does not guarantee. And Allah, Glorified and Exalted, knows best.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a corrupt lease (ijara fasida) caused by a condition that contradicts the contract, specifically when a hired tailor deviates from the instructions given by the cloth owner. The rule is that a condition that is not part of the contract's requirements corrupts the lease, and in such a case, the worker is entitled to the market rate (ujrat al-mithl) for his work, but this wage cannot exceed the amount that was originally specified (musamma) in the contract. The commentator explains the example: if a tailor is told to cut a qaba (a type of coat) but he instead cuts a qamis (a shirt), the owner has two options. He may either accept the qaba and pay the market wage, or reject it and demand the value of the cloth (because the tailor acted contrary to orders). The reasoning is that the qaba resembles a qamis in some respects (since Turks use it like a shirt), so there is partial conformity. The owner may choose the side of agreement (taking the qaba with market wage) or the side of deviation (claiming the cloth's value). The market wage is obligatory instead of the named wage because the owner only consented to the named wage when the intended purpose was fully achieved, and it was not. The ruling is general, covering both cases where the work is used as a qamis and where it is split and made into a qaba. This is contrary to al-Asbajabi, who, in the second case, imposes liability without giving the owner an option. The passage also notes that if they disagree about what was ordered, the word of the cloth owner is taken. The same ruling applies if the tailor makes a sirwal (trousers) instead of a qaba. Then the author quotes from al-Khulasa: if a dyer dyes the cloth yellow instead of red, the owner may either claim the value of a white cloth (implying full compensation) or take the dyed cloth and pay the increase in value due to the dye, but the dyer receives no wage. If the dye is defective but not excessively so, there is no liability; if it is excessive by the standard of craftsmen, the dyer guarantees the value of a white cloth. Other examples include a tailor who cuts the cloth too short: if the deficiency is minor (like a finger's length), it is disregarded; if more, he guarantees. Also, if the tailor is asked to check if the cloth is sufficient for a qamis and then cuts, he is liable if he incorrectly said it suffices; but if he first confirms sufficiency and then cuts and it turns out insufficient, he is not liable. These examples illustrate the principle that in a fasid lease, the worker is not entitled to the agreed wage but to the market rate, and the owner has options depending on the degree of deviation.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, determined by the prevailing rate for the service rendered.
المسمى (al-musamma): The wage explicitly named and agreed upon in the lease contract.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijara al-fasida): A lease contract that is valid in its origin but defective in its description, typically due to a condition or uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tailor example, if the owner chooses to take the qaba (the made garment), what must he pay?
A) The named wage (musamma) because the tailor did some work.
B) Ujrat al-mithl (market rate) not exceeding the named wage.
C) Nothing, because the tailor deviated.
D) The full value of the cloth, because the tailor's work is worthless.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid lease, the worker deserves ujrat al-mithl capped by the named wage, and the owner has options based on the degree of deviation.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Fasid Lease and Invalidating Conditions
Definition, distinction, and conditions of fasid lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a fasid lease, distinguish it from a batil lease, identify conditions that invalidate it, and apply the rule of ujrat al-mithl.

Core Idea
A fasid lease is valid in origin but defective in description; it obligates ujrat al-mithl, not the named wage if unknown or unlawful.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every defective contract is void. Some contracts, like a fasid lease, remain valid in essence but become corrupt due to a condition or uncertainty. This lesson unpacks the definition of fasid lease, clarifies how it differs from batil, and lists the specific conditions that render a lease fasid. You will also learn the crucial rule of ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) — the compensation due in such contracts.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate fasid from batil
Understand that a fasid contract is prescribed in its origin (asl) but not in its description (wasf), while a batil contract is not prescribed at all. Note the consequence: a fasid lease obligates ujrat al-mithl upon use, a batil lease obligates nothing.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the invalidating conditions
Examine the list of conditions that corrupt the lease: those not part of muqtada al-'aqd (the contract's natural requirements). Conditions like requiring the tenant to make repairs, pay taxes, or bear uncertain risks make the lease fasid.
The maxim: 'Every uncertainty that corrupts a sale also corrupts a lease.'
3
Apply al-Karkhi's maxim
Memorize the four areas of uncertainty that corrupt: the subject matter, the wage, the duration, or the work itself. Any jihala (uncertainty) in these makes the lease fasid.
This is a key test for evaluating lease contracts.
4
Understand the rule of ujrat al-mithl
In a fasid lease, the lessee must pay ujrat al-mithl (fair market wage) for the benefit received. This amount cannot exceed the named wage unless the named wage is unknown or unlawful (e.g., wine or pork).
The named wage creates a semblance of a contract up to its amount.
5
Apply to contemporary examples
Use the principles to evaluate modern leases. For instance, leasing waqf land with the condition that the tenant pays taxes is fasid. Similarly, any lease with a condition that contradicts the natural purpose (e.g., not to live in the house) is fasid.
The mufta bihi position is clear: such conditions invalidate the lease.

وهي كل عقد كان مشروعاً بأصله دون وصفه. وبين الفاسد والباطل هنا فرق أيضاً فإن الباطل ما ليس بمشروع أصلاً وحكمه أنه لا يجب فيه بالاستعمال أجر بخلاف الفاسد فإنه يجب فيه به أجرة المثل؛ صرح به في الحقائق شرح المنظومة في مسألة إجارة المشاع، وهكذا في جامع الفضولين لكن بين الإجارة والبيع فرق فإن الفاسد من البيع يملك بالقبض

والفاسد من الإجارة لا يملك المنافع بالقبض حتى لو قبضها المستأجر ليس له أن يؤاجرها، ولو أجرها وجب أجر المثل ولا يكون غاصباً وللآجر الأول أن ينقض هذه الإجارة؛ كذا في الخلاصة قوله : (يفسد الإجارة الشرط) أي الشروط المعهودة المتقدمة في باب البيع الفاسد التي ليست من مقتضى العقد لا كل شرط لأن الإجارة عقد معاوضة محضة تقال وتفسخ فكانت كالبيع، فكل ما أفسد البيع أفسدها. وقد ضبطه الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي في مختصره فقال : إذا كان ما وقع عليه عقد الإجارة مجهولاً في نفسه أو في أجرة أو في مدة الإجارة أو في العمل المستأجر عليه فالإجارة فاسدة، وكل جهالة تدخل في البيع فتفسده من جهة الجهالة فكذلك هي في الإجارة ا هـ . والشروط التي تفسدها تفصيلاً كاشتراط تطيين الدار ومرمتها أو تعليق باب عليها أو إدخال جذع في سقفها على المستأجر، وكذا اشتراط كري نهر في الأرض أو ضرب مسناة عليها أو حفر بئر فيها أو أن يسرقنها على وعليه أجر مثل ما سار عليها وكذا لو استأجر عبداً شهراً على أنه إنه مرض فيه عمل في الشهر الذي بعده بقدر الأيام التي مرض فيها؛ كذا في غاية البيان. فخرج ما يقتضيه العقد كاشتراط أن يدفع له الأجر إذا رجع من وفيما زاد عليه لم يوجد فيه عقد ولا شبهة فبقي على الأصل. وأشار بعدم مجاوزته للمسمى إلى أن الكلام فيما إذا كان المسمى معلوماً غير محرم لأنه لو كان الفساد الجهالة المسمى كله أو بعضه أو لعدمه ليس فيه مسمى حتى يصح أن تنتفي المجاوزة عنه فلهذا وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ، وكذا لو كان الأجر خمراً أو خنزيراً فإنه يجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ واستثنى الشارح أيضاً ما إذا استأجر داراً على أن لا يسكنها فالإجارة Chapter of Fasid Lease: It is every contract that is prescribed in its origin but not in its description. And between fasid and batil here there is also a difference: batil is that which is not prescribed at all, and its ruling is that no wage is obligatory by use, unlike fasid, for which the equivalent wage is obligatory by use; it is declared in al-Haqaiq Sharh al-Manzooma regarding the issue of joint lease, and similarly in Jami' al-Fudulayn, but between lease and sale there is a difference: the fasid of sale is owned by possession... (poetic lines)... The fasid of lease does not own the usufruct by possession, so if the lessee takes possession, he may not sublease it; if he does sublease it, the equivalent wage is obligatory, and he is not a usurper, and the first lessor may cancel this lease; thus in al-Khulasa. His statement: (The condition corrupts the lease) i.e. the familiar conditions mentioned in the chapter on corrupt sale that are not part of the requirements of the contract, not every condition, because lease is a pure commutative contract that is invalidated and dissolved, so it is like sale; thus everything that corrupts a sale corrupts it. And Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi defined it in his Mukhtasar saying: If what the lease contract is concluded upon is unknown in itself, or in the wage, or in the duration of the lease, or in the work hired for, then the lease is fasid, and every uncertainty that enters a sale and corrupts it due to uncertainty likewise is in the lease. End quote. And the conditions that corrupt it in detail include: stipulating that the tenant plaster the house and repair it, or install a door on it, or insert a beam in its ceiling; likewise stipulating that the tenant dig a canal in the land, or build a dam on it, or dig a well in it, or that he steal it; and likewise stipulating that the land be returned tilled; and likewise if he stipulates that if the water stops from the mill, the wage is upon him; and likewise if he hires a mount to Baghdad on condition that if he earns something, he gives it, and if he reaches Baghdad, he gets such-and-such, otherwise nothing; it is fasid, and he owes the equivalent wage for what he traveled; and likewise if he hires a slave for a month on condition that if he falls ill during it, he works in the following month for the days he was ill; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. This excludes what the contract requires, such as stipulating that he pay the wage when he returns from travel, and stipulating that he vacate the premises for him today. And in al-Khulasa, quoting from the original: If one rents a house on condition that the tenant maintain it and pay its taxes, it is corrupt because it is a condition contrary to the requirements of the contract. End quote. So it is known from this that what occurs in our time of leasing waqf land for a known wage on condition that the taxes and the cost of the inspector are upon the tenant, or that the erosion is upon the tenant, is corrupt, as is not hidden. His statement: (And he has its equivalent wage not exceeding the named) because the fasid is annexed to the valid, so in the amount of the named there is a semblance of a contract, but in what exceeds it there is no contract or semblance, so it remains on the original principle. And his indication by not exceeding the named is that the discussion is when the named is known and not prohibited, because if the corruption is due to uncertainty of the named, in whole or in part, or its non-existence, there is no named such that the non-exceeding can be negated; therefore the equivalent wage is obligatory, whatever it reaches. Likewise if the wage was wine or swine, the equivalent wage is obligatory, whatever it reaches. And the commentator also excepted the case where one rents a house on condition that he not live in it; the lease is fasid, and if he lives in it, the equivalent wage is obligatory, whatever it reaches, and there is consideration in this, because the wage, if it is not... (colophon): For as long as the nightingale sings melodiously and our joys renew the seal of the sea. That was in the beginning of Rabi' al-Thani in the year 1230 AH. And I, the poor in need of Him, the least of His servants and the most in need of His support and guidance, Muhammad Amin ibn 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad, known as Ibn 'Abidin, may he be forgiven. Amen.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the nature of a fasid (corrupt) lease, together with a detailed enumeration of conditions that invalidate it. The author first defines a fasid lease as a contract that is valid in its origin (because it is of a type recognized by Shari'ah) but defective in its description (due to a condition or uncertainty that does not nullify its essence). He distinguishes it from a batil (void) lease, which is not valid at all and does not incur any wage even if used. In contrast, a fasid lease obligates ujrat al-mithl (the market wage) when the lessee benefits from the property. The author notes that in a fasid lease, the lessee does not own the usufruct merely by taking possession; therefore, he cannot sublease the property. If he does sublease, the sublessee owes ujrat al-mithl, and the original lessor has the right to cancel the first lease. Then the commentary explains the ruling 'The condition corrupts the lease' by clarifying that it refers to conditions that are not part of the contract's natural requirements (muqtada al-'aqd). Since lease is a commutative contract like sale, any condition that would corrupt a sale also corrupts a lease. Al-Karkhi's maxim is cited: uncertainty (jihala) in the subject matter, wage, duration, or the work itself renders the lease fasid. The passage lists numerous specific invalidating conditions: requiring the tenant to plaster and repair the house, install a door, insert a beam, dig a canal, build a dam, dig a well, return the land tilled, bear the risk of water shortage for a mill, or making the wage conditional on uncertain events like earnings during travel or on reaching a destination. Similarly, if a slave is hired with a condition to make up missed work due to illness, it is fasid. On the other hand, conditions that are inherent to the contract, like payment upon return from travel or vacation of premises at a certain time, are valid. Applying this to contemporary practice (of the author's time), leasing waqf land with the condition that the tenant bears taxes and costs is fasid. Finally, the passage returns to the earlier ruling about ujrat al-mithl not exceeding the named wage. The rationale is that a fasid contract is analogized to a valid one only up to the amount of the named wage, because there is a semblance (shubha) of a contract in that amount. Beyond the named wage, there is no contract or semblance, so the default principle of no compensation applies. However, this limitation applies only when the named wage is known and lawful. If the corruption is due to uncertainty in the wage, if the wage is completely unknown or if it is a prohibited substance like wine or pork, then ujrat al-mithl is due in full without regard to the named wage. The commentator also mentions an exception: if one rents a house on condition that he not live in it, and then he does live in it, ujrat al-mithl is due in full, though there is some debate on this point. The passage ends with the scribe's notes, including the date (1230 AH) and the name of Ibn 'Abidin.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijara al-fasida): A lease contract that is valid in its origin (asl) because it is a recognized transaction, but defective in its description (wasf) due to a condition or uncertainty.
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for the benefit received, determined by the prevailing rate for similar services or property.
الشرط المخالف لمقتضى العقد (al-shart al-mukhalif li-muqtada al-'aqd): A condition that contradicts the essential purpose or natural consequences of the contract, e.g., requiring the tenant to perform repairs that are the landlord's responsibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone rents a house on the condition that the tenant will not live in it, and then the tenant does live in it, what is the ruling?
A) The lease is valid, and the named rent is due.
B) The lease is fasid, and ujrat al-mithl is due in full without regard to the named rent.
C) The lease is batil, and no rent is due.
D) The lease is fasid, but the named rent is due because the tenant breached the condition.

Key Takeaway
A fasid lease obligates ujrat al-mithl for actual use; the named wage is a ceiling only if known and lawful; conditions contrary to muqtada al-'aqd corrupt the lease.

Conditions Invalidating Ijarah and Ujrat al-Mithl
Commentary on conditions invalidating ijarah and ujrat al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify conditions that invalidate ijarah and apply the Hanafi rule for ujrat al-mithl in both valid and invalid leases.

Core Idea
A condition not inherent to the contract that introduces uncertainty invalidates ijarah; ujrat al-mithl is paid but cannot exceed the valid named rent.

This lesson unpacks a key passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, where Ibn Nujaym explains which conditions invalidate a lease (ijarah) and how the lessee must compensate the lessor when the lease is invalid. The Hanafi school treats ijarah like a sale because both are pure commutative contracts, so the same rules about invalidating conditions apply. Through detailed examples and a qiyas (analogy) to sale, you will learn to distinguish between permissible inherent conditions and those that make the contract fasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
State the ijarah contract and the specific condition in question (e.g., tenant must repair the roof). Recognize that the condition may be inherent or extraneous.
2
Classify the condition
Determine if the condition is inherent to the contract (muqtada al-aqd) or extraneous. Inherent conditions, like payment of rent at a specified time, are valid. Extraneous ones that are not part of the natural exchange are suspect.
The passage emphasizes 'laysat min muqtada al-aqd'.
3
Apply qiyas to sale
Since ijarah is a pure commutative contract (muawadah mahdah), any condition that would invalidate a sale also invalidates ijarah. Use the examples from sale (e.g., unknown price) as a benchmark.
Qiyas jali: both contracts share the illa of being commutative and subject to annulment.
4
Check for uncertainty (jihalah)
Does the condition create uncertainty about the rent, term, object, or work? Uncertainty that leads to dispute invalidates the contract. Refer to al-Karkhi's definition.
If the condition is known and fixed, it may be permissible if it's inherent.
5
Determine the consequence
If the contract is fasid, the lessee does not own the benefits by mere possession and cannot sublease. The lessee must pay ujrat al-mithl (equivalent rent), limited to the named rent if it was known and lawful. If the named rent is unknown or unlawful, ujrat al-mithl is due without limit.
The original lessor has the right to cancel the lease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفاسد من الإجارة لا يملك المنافع بالقبض حتى لو قبضها المستأجر ليس له أن يؤاجرها، ولو أجرها وجب أجر المثل ولا يكون غاصباً وللآجر الأول أن ينقض هذه الإجارة؛ كذا في الخلاصة قوله : (يفسد الإجارة الشرط) أي الشروط المعهودة المتقدمة في باب البيع الفاسد التي ليست من مقتضى العقد لا كل شرط لأن الإجارة عقد معاوضة محضة تقال وتفسخ فكانت كالبيع، فكل ما أفسد البيع أفسدها. وقد ضبطه الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي في مختصره فقال : إذا كان ما وقع عليه عقد الإجارة مجهولاً في نفسه أو في أجرة أو في مدة الإجارة أو في العمل المستأجر عليه فالإجارة فاسدة، وكل جهالة تدخل في البيع فتفسده من جهة الجهالة فكذلك هي في الإجارة ا هـ . والشروط التي تفسدها تفصيلاً كاشتراط تطيين الدار ومرمتها أو تعليق باب عليها أو إدخال جذع في سقفها على المستأجر، وكذا اشتراط كري نهر في الأرض أو ضرب مسناة عليها أو حفر بئر فيها أو أن يسرقنها على المستأجر، وكذلك اشتراط رد الأرض مكروبة، وكذا لو شرط إن انقطع الماء عن الرحى فالأجر عليه، وكذا إن تكارى دابة إلى بغداد أو على أنه إن رزق شيئاً أعطاه وإن بلغت بغداد فله كذا وإلا فلا شيء له فهي فاسدة وعليه أجر مثل ما سار عليها وكذا لو استأجر عبداً شهراً على أنه إنه مرض فيه عمل في الشهر الذي بعده بقدر الأيام التي مرض فيها؛ كذا في غاية البيان. فخرج ما يقتضيه العقد كاشتراط أن يدفع له الأجر إذا رجع من السفر، واشتراط أن يفرغ له اليوم. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى الأصل: لو استأجر داراً على أن يعمرها ويعطي نوائبها تفسد لأنه شرط مخالف لمقتضى العقد ا هـ . فعلم بهذا أن ما يقع في زماننا من إجارة أرض الوقف بأجرة معلومة على أن المغارم وكلفة الكاشف على المستأجر أو على أن الجرف على المستأجر فاسد كما لا يخفى قوله : ( وله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به (المسمى لأن الفاسد ملحق بالصحيح فوجد في قدر المسمى شبهة العقد وفيما زاد عليه لم يوجد فيه عقد ولا شبهة فبقي على الأصل. وأشار بعدم مجاوزته للمسمى إلى أن الكلام فيما إذا كان المسمى معلوماً غير محرم لأنه لو كان الفساد الجهالة المسمى كله أو بعضه أو لعدمه ليس فيه مسمى حتى يصح أن تنتفي المجاوزة عنه فلهذا وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ، وكذا لو كان الأجر خمراً أو خنزيراً فإنه يجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ واستثنى الشارح أيضاً ما إذا استأجر داراً على أن لا يسكنها فالإجارة فاسدة ويجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ إن سكنها وفيه نظر، لأن الأجرة إن لم تكن مسماة فهي المسألة المتقدمة وإن كانت مسماة ينبغي أن لا يجاوز به المسمى كغيرها من الشروط، وقد ذكرها في الخلاصة ولم يتعرض للأجرة ثم قال: وإن شرط أن يسكنها المستأجر وحده يجوز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب. وهذا آخر ما نظمه بنان التحقيق في سمط الدراري وتحلى به عقود البيان ففاق اللآلئ في جيد الجواري، ونهاية ما الله تأليفه للعلامة الفاضل والأستاذ الكامل الشيخ زين الدين الشهير بابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى وغفر الله لنا وله ولكل المسلمين أجمعين آمين والحمد الله رب العالمين.
And the invalid (fasid) from ijarah: he does not own the benefits by taking possession such that if the lessee took possession he is not allowed to sublease it; and if he leased it, he must pay the equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl) and he is not a usurper, and the original lessor has the right to cancel this lease; thus in al-Khulasa. His statement: (The condition invalidates the lease) refers to the usual conditions mentioned in the chapter on invalid sale that are not inherent to the contract, not every condition, because lease is a pure commutative contract that may be contested and canceled, so it is like a sale. Therefore, everything that invalidates a sale invalidates it. Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi defined it in his Mukhtasar: If that which the lease contract is concluded upon is unknown (majhul) in itself, or in its rent, or in its term, or in the work for which the worker is hired, then the lease is invalid. Every uncertainty that enters a sale and invalidates it due to uncertainty similarly applies in ijarah. The conditions that invalidate it in detail include: stipulating that the tenant is responsible for plastering and repairing the house, or hanging a door, or inserting a beam into its ceiling; similarly stipulating that the tenant is to dig a canal in the land, or build a dyke, or dig a well, or irrigate it; likewise stipulating returning the land cultivated (makruba); similarly if he stipulates that if the water stops from the mill then the rent is on him; likewise if he hires a mount to Baghdad on condition that if he acquires something he gives it to him, or if he reaches Baghdad he gets such and such, otherwise nothing, it is invalid and he owes the equivalent rent for what he traveled; similarly if he hires a slave for a month on condition that if he falls ill during it he will work in the following month for the days he was ill; thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. Excluded are what the contract inherently requires, like stipulating that he pay the rent when he returns from travel, or stipulating that he vacate for him today. In al-Khulasa citing al-Asl: if he hires a house on condition that he maintain it and pay its taxes, it is invalid because it is a condition contrary to the inherent nature of the contract. From this it is known that what occurs in our time of leasing awqaf land for a known rent on condition that the expenses and cost of the inspector fall on the lessee, or that the riverbank maintenance is on the lessee, is invalid as is not hidden. His statement: (He owes its equivalent rent not exceeding the named rent) because the invalid is attached to the valid, so in the amount of the named rent there is a semblance (shubha) of the contract, and in what exceeds that there is no contract nor semblance, so it remains on the original principle. By saying 'not exceeding the named' he indicates that the discussion is when the named rent is known and not unlawful, because if the invalidity is due to uncertainty of the named rent wholly or partially, or its absence, there is no named rent such that exceeding it could be negated; hence the equivalent rent is due whatever it may be. Similarly if the rent is wine or a pig, the equivalent rent is due whatever it may be. The commentator also excepted the case of hiring a house on condition that he not live in it; the lease is invalid and he owes the equivalent rent whatever it may be if he lived in it; there is consideration (nazar) because if the rent was not named then it is the previous issue; if it was named, then it should not exceed the named rent like other conditions. Al-Khulasa mentioned it but did not discuss the rent; then he said: and if he stipulates that the lessee alone lives in it, it is permissible. And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and resort. This is the last of what the pen of investigation composed on the string of pearls, adorned with the necklaces of elucidation, surpassing pearls on the necks of maidens, and the completion of what Allah finished of the composition of the distinguished scholar and perfect master, Shaykh Zayn al-Din known as Ibn Nujaym, may Allah have mercy on him, forgive us and him and all Muslims, Ameen, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn statement 'يفسد الإجارة الشرط' (the condition invalidates the lease) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains that the conditions referred to are those that are not inherent to the contract (laysat min muqtada al-aqd) and were previously mentioned in the chapter on invalid sale. He compares ijarah to sale because both are pure commutative contracts (muawadah mahdah) that can be annulled, so the same rules apply. He then cites al-Karkhi's definition: uncertainty (jihalah) in the object, rent, term, or work invalidates the lease. The commentary provides detailed examples: stipulating repairs, digging, etc., which are contrary to the nature of ijarah. It also addresses practical cases like leasing waqf land with extra costs on the tenant, ruling it invalid. The second part discusses the ruling on ujrat al-mithl (equivalent rent) for an invalid lease. The general rule: if the named rent is known and lawful, the lessee must pay ujrat al-mithl not exceeding that named rent. But if the invalidity is due to uncertainty or illegality of the named rent, then ujrat al-mithl is due without limit. The commentator also mentions an exception for a lease where the tenant is prohibited from living in the house, and then argues that if the rent was named, it should still apply. Finally, the passage concludes with a poetic flourish and the completion of the Ijarah section of al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A lease contract that is invalid due to a condition that introduces uncertainty or contradicts the inherent nature of the contract
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The rental value of a similar property or service in the market
الجهالة (al-jihalah): Uncertainty or lack of knowledge about an essential element of the contract (e.g., rent, term, object)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is ujrat al-mithl (equivalent rent) owed without limitation (i.e., it may exceed the named rent) in an invalid ijarah contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the named rent is known and lawful.
B) When the named rent is unknown or unlawful, e.g., wine or pig.
C) When the lessee actually takes possession.
D) When the contract is silent about rent.

Key Takeaway
A condition that is not part of the inherent exchange and introduces uncertainty invalidates ijarah; ujrat al-mithl is paid but capped by the valid named rent.
